[4:2:352,476] independent entities under the California 

[4:3:352,485] Constitution, or are departments with a 

[4:4:352,494] recognized need to operate outside of the 

[5:0:352,503] administrative oversight and control of an agency 

[5:1:352,512] secretary. Constitutionally-established bodies 

[5:2:352,521] include the Legislature, Judicial Branch, 

[5:3:352,530] Governor's Office, and constitutional officers. 

[5:4:352,539] This section also includes such independent 

[5:5:352,548] entities as the Inspector General and the 

[5:6:352,557] California State Lottery.

[1:0:266,44] 0110 Senate 

[2:0:58,64] The Legislature is comprised of two houses, the Senate and the Assembly, and is responsible for enacting laws and 

[2:1:58,73] establishing public policy for California. The State Senate is comprised of 40 members who are elected for 4-year terms. 

[2:2:58,82] Members of the Legislature may serve a maximum of 12 years total in the Senate, the Assembly, or both, in any 

[2:3:58,91] combination of terms. Members first elected before June 6, 2012, however, may generally serve a maximum of 14 years 

[2:4:58,100] total, with no more than two terms in the Senate and three terms in the Assembly.

[6:0:137,259] 0150 Contributions to the Legislators' Retirement System 

[6:1:58,279] Established in 1947, the Legislators' Retirement System provides retirement and death benefits for legislators, constitutional 

[6:2:58,288] officers, and legislative statutory officers. 

[7:0:58,306] The Legislators' Retirement System is funded through contributions from the state, members of the system, and investment 

[7:1:58,315] earnings. Between 2000-01 and 2011-12, the Legislators' Retirement System was super-funded and neither the state nor 

[7:2:58,324] members were required to contribute. Beginning in 2012-13, contributions resumed for the state and members. 

[7:3:58,342] The California Public Employees' Retirement System (CalPERS) administers the Legislators' Retirement System on behalf 

[7:4:58,351] of its members. Retirement benefits paid are based upon age, years of service, and final compensation. Benefits for death, 

[7:5:58,360] disability, and surviving dependents of deceased members are also provided under specific conditions. 

[7:6:58,378] Proposition 140, approved by voters in 1990, closed the Legislators' Retirement System to all new legislators after 

[7:7:58,387] November 6, 1990. 

[8:0:58,405] Effective January 1, 2013, the Legislators' Retirement System was closed to all new members by the California Public 

[8:1:58,414] Employees' Pension Reform Act of 2013, Chapter 296, Statutes of 2012 (AB 340). New constitutional officers, statutory 

[8:2:58,423] officers, Sergeant-at-Arms, and the Insurance Commissioner retain optional membership rights in CalPERS.

[5:0:207,237] 0160 Legislative Counsel Bureau 

[5:1:58,257] The Legislative Counsel Bureau (Bureau) provides legal assistance to the two houses of the Legislature, and their members 

[5:2:58,266] and committees, by resolving a large volume of complex legal problems arising in connection with the legislative process. 

[5:3:58,275] The legal services furnished include rendering opinions, drafting bills, counseling, attending as counsel meetings of 

[5:4:58,284] legislative committees, and representing the Legislature in litigation. The attorney-client relationship is maintained and all 

[5:5:58,293] work is confidential. 

[6:0:58,311] In addition, the Bureau prepares and provides necessary indices and appropriate tables necessary to identify legislative 

[6:1:58,320] measures and compiles and indexes statutes and codes. 

[7:0:58,338] The Bureau operates the Legislative Data Center, which provides information technology services in support of the 

[7:1:58,347] legislative information system and the processing of legislative measures. 

[8:0:58,365] Pursuant to Chapter 46 of the Statutes of 2012, the California Commission on Uniform State Laws was transferred into the 

[8:1:58,374] Legislative Counsel Bureau. The California Commission on Uniform State Laws presents to the Legislature uniform laws 

[8:2:58,383] recommended by the National Conference of Commissioners on Uniform State Laws and then promotes passage of these 

[8:3:58,392] uniform acts.

[8:0:241,435] 0250 Judicial Branch 

[8:1:58,456] Article VI of the Constitution creates the Supreme Court of California and the Courts of Appeal to exercise the judicial power 

[8:2:58,465] of the state at the appellate level. Article VI also creates the Judicial Council of California to administer the state's judicial 

[8:3:58,474] system. Chapter 869, Statutes of 1997, created the California Habeas Corpus Resource Center to represent any person 

[8:4:58,483] financially unable to employ appellate counsel in capital cases. 

[9:0:58,501] The Lockyer-Isenberg Trial Court Funding Act of 1997 (Chapter 850, Statutes of 1997) provided a stable and consistent 

[9:1:58,510] funding source for the trial courts. Beginning with fiscal year 1997-98, consolidation of the costs of operation of the trial 

[9:2:58,519] courts was implemented at the state level, with the exception of facility, revenue collection, and local judicial benefit costs. 

[9:3:58,528] This implementation capped the counties' general purpose revenue contributions to trial court costs at a revised 1994-95 

[9:4:58,537] level. The county contributions become part of the Trial Court Trust Fund, which supports all trial court operations. Fine and 

[9:5:58,546] penalty revenue collected by each county is retained or distributed in accordance with statute. Each county makes quarterly 

[9:6:58,555] payments to the Trial Court Trust Fund equal to the fine and penalty revenue received by the state General Fund in 1994-95, 

[9:7:58,564] as adjusted by amounts equivalent to specified fine and fee revenues that counties benefited from in 2003-04. The Trial 

[9:8:58,573] Court Facilities Act of 2002 (Chapter 1082, Statutes of 2002) provided a process for the responsibility for court facilities to be 

[9:9:58,582] transferred from the counties to the state by July 1, 2007, which was extended to December 31, 2009, by Chapter 9, 

[10:0:58,591] Statutes of 2008. The Trial Court Facilities Act of 2002 also established several new revenue sources, which went into effect 

[10:1:58,600] on January 1, 2003. These revenues are deposited into the State Court Facilities Construction Fund for the purpose of 

[10:2:58,609] funding the construction and maintenance of court facilities throughout the state. Counties contribute revenues for the 

[11:0:58,618] ongoing operation and maintenance of court facilities based upon historical expenditures for facilities transferred to the state. 

[11:1:58,636] The mission of the Judicial Branch is to resolve disputes arising under the law and to interpret and apply the law 

[12:0:58,645] consistently, impartially, and independently to protect the rights and liberties guaranteed by the Constitutions of California 

[12:1:58,654] and the United States, in a fair, accessible, effective, and efficient manner. 

[13:0:58,672] Because the Judicial Branch's programs drive a need for infrastructure investment, the Judicial Branch has a capital outlay 

[13:1:58,681] program to support this need. For the specifics on the Judicial Branch's capital outlay program see "Infrastructure Overview."

[10:0:55,194] 1/ Includes all Program 0150 "State Trial Court Funding" as well as Program 0140019 "Trial Court Operations" expenses from all funds, including the Trial Court Trust Fund (TCTF), State Trial Court Improvement and Modernization Fund (IMF),  

[10:1:55,202] General Fund (GF), and Judicial Branch Workers' Compensation Fund (JBWCF). The expenses do not necessarily represent all expenses as those programs have a state operations component (e.g., Equal Access Fund) and/or a distribution that is  

[10:2:55,209] made directly to courts (e.g., court-appointed dependency counsel). 

[11:0:55,219] 2/ These expenses are funded by the trial courts opting to participate in those programs from their "State Funding" revenue distribution amounts reported in Section 1 of the "State and Non-State Trial Court Funding, Expenditures, and Positions"  

[11:1:55,226] display. Because the funding for these expenses is already included in Section 1, they are subtracted from the total "State Trial Court Funding Not Distributed to the Trial Courts" amount used to calculate the total expenditures displayed for "State  

[11:2:55,233] Trial Court Funding Total".  

[12:0:55,243] 3/ This reflects judges' compensation paid excluding any amounts related to the reimbursement of courts for payments of judges' compensation as these amounts are already included in the courts' "State Funding" revenue amounts reported in the  

[12:1:55,251] Trial Court Information section ($113.5 million in 2015-16 and $119.1 million in 2016-17). Judges from the Los Angeles, Riverside, and Ventura County Superior Courts are compensated locally and the court/county is reimbursed by the TCTF. In  

[12:2:55,257] addition, 26 courts in 2015-16 and 25 courts in 2016-17 participate in the local salary reimbursement program in which a small portion of the judges' salary is paid locally and reimbursed by the TCTF. 

[13:0:55,273] 4/ Reflects actual or estimated payments made directly to court-appointed dependency counsel from the TCTF on behalf of superior courts participating in the Dependency Representation, Administration, Funding, and Training (DRAFT) Program.  

[13:1:55,281] Courts not participating in the DRAFT program are reimbursed up to a maximum amount from the TCTF for payments to court-appointed dependency counsel. 

[14:0:55,292] 5/ For the TCTF, expenses are the annual premiums for 57 participating trial courts from their allocations and for superior court judges from the appropriation for the Compensation of Superior Court Judges that are transferred to the JBWCF. For  

[14:1:55,299] the JBWCF, these expenses reflect payments of trial court employee and judge related workers' compensation claims from the JBWCF less the amount transferred from the TCTF.

[0:0:58,15] LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE   2017-18 STATE BUDGET — LJE 21 

[1:0:206,44] 0250 Judicial Branch - Continued 

[2:0:58,82] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[3:0:58,109] 0130 - SUPREME COURT 

[4:0:58,127] The Supreme Court is the highest court in the California judicial system. Its decisions are binding on all other California 

[4:1:58,136] state courts. The Chief Justice of California and the six Associate Justices entertain petitions seeking review of decisions 

[4:2:58,145] from the Courts of Appeal, original petitions for extraordinary relief (such as writs of mandate or habeas corpus), and 

[4:3:58,154] recommendations for discipline of judicial officers and attorneys. The Court grants review and issues opinions in order to 

[4:4:58,163] settle legal questions of statewide importance. In addition, under the California Constitution, all death penalty judgments are 

[4:5:58,172] appealed directly to the Supreme Court. 

[5:0:58,190] 0135 - COURTS OF APPEAL 

[6:0:58,208] Established by a constitutional amendment in 1904, the Courts of Appeal are California's intermediate courts of review. The 

[6:1:58,217] six District Courts of Appeal hear appeals and original proceedings at nine different locations around the state. Cases 

[6:2:58,226] before the Courts of Appeal involve every area of civil and criminal law. 

[7:0:58,244] 0140 - JUDICIAL COUNCIL 

[8:0:58,262] The Judicial Council of California is the constitutional policy-making body for the state judiciary. The Council consists of 21 

[8:1:58,271] voting members and 11 advisory members; the Chief Justice of California serves as chair. The Judicial Council staff serve 

[8:2:58,280] as the administrative arm of the Council. Staff provide policy support to the Council, administrative accountability in the 

[8:3:58,289] operation of the courts as specified by law, strategic planning for capital outlay, design, and construction of court facilities; 

[8:4:58,298] and administrative support for courts in areas such as budget, fiscal services, coordination of the assignment of retired 

[8:5:58,307] judges, technology, education, legal advice and services, human resources, legislative advocacy, and research. 

[9:0:58,325] Consistent with the judiciary's mission, the Judicial Council is guided by the following principles: 

[10:0:58,341] • 

[10:1:58,350] • 

[11:0:68,343] To make decisions in the best interests of the public and the court system as a whole. 

[12:0:68,352] To conduct the Council's business based on an underlying commitment to equal and timely justice and public access to 

[12:1:68,361] an independent forum for the resolution of disputes. 

[13:0:58,368] • 

[14:0:68,370] To provide leadership in the administration of justice by planning and advocating for policies and resources that are 

[14:1:68,379] necessary for courts to fulfill their mission. 

[15:0:58,386] • 

[16:0:68,388] To ensure the continued development of an accessible, independent court system through planning, research, and 

[16:1:68,397] evaluation programs, and through the use of modern management approaches and technological developments. 

[16:2:68,406] To provide leadership in the administration of justice by establishing broad and consistent policies for the operation of the 

[16:3:68,415] courts and appropriate uniform statewide rules and forms. 

[17:0:58,404] • 

[18:0:58,422] • 

[19:0:68,424] To promote a competent, responsive, and ethical judiciary and staff through a comprehensive program of judicial 

[19:1:68,433] education and training for court employees. 

[20:0:58,440] • 

[20:1:58,449] • 

[21:0:68,442] To contribute to the public's understanding of the judicial process through a continuing program of public education. 

[21:1:68,451] To provide assistance to the courts in developing action plans that are consistent with the Council's Strategic Plan and 

[21:2:68,460] that address local needs and priorities. 

[22:0:58,478] 0140023 - JUDICIAL BRANCH FACILITY PROGRAM 

[23:0:58,496] The Judicial Branch Facility Program administers the acquisition, planning, construction, operations, and maintenance of 

[23:1:58,505] judicial branch facilities. This program is responsible for the development of long-term facilities master plans, facility and 

[23:2:58,514] real estate management, and new courthouse planning, design, and construction. 

[24:0:58,532] 0150 - STATE TRIAL COURT FUNDING 

[25:0:58,550] 0150010 - SUPPORT FOR THE OPERATION OF THE TRIAL COURTS 

[26:0:58,568] This program's objective is to provide the resources necessary for the statewide trial court system to adjudicate civil and 

[26:1:58,577] criminal cases. This program includes all allowable trial court administrative costs under Government Code section 77003, 

[26:2:58,586] except court-appointed dependency counsel, salaries and benefits of Superior Court judges, compensation for assigned 

[26:3:58,595] judges, support for language interpreters, grants, and expenses on behalf of the trial courts. 

[27:0:58,613] 0150011 - COURT APPOINTED DEPENDENCY COUNSEL 

[28:0:58,631] This program provides funding for court-appointed counsel in juvenile court dependency proceedings and counsel appointed 

[28:1:58,640] by the court to represent a minor pursuant to Chapter 10 (commencing with Section 3150) of Part 2 of Division 8 of the 

[28:2:58,649] Family Code. 

[29:0:58,667] 0150019 - COMPENSATION OF SUPERIOR COURT JUDGES 

[30:0:58,685] This program provides funding for the salaries and state benefits for Superior Court judges. 

[31:0:58,703] 0150028 - ASSIGNED JUDGES 

[32:0:58,721] This program provides support for the salaries and related costs of retired as well as active judges who are assigned by the 

[33:0:58,745] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[2:2:58,100] 0150037 - COURT INTERPRETERS 

[3:0:58,118] This program supports the provision of qualified language interpreters in criminal, juvenile, family and civil proceedings as 

[3:1:58,127] required by statute. 

[3:2:58,145] 0150046 - GRANTS 

[4:0:58,163] This program provides funding for government grants providing public services related to the trial courts. 

[4:1:58,181] 0150095 - EXPENSES ON BEHALF OF THE TRIAL COURTS 

[5:0:58,199] This program provides appropriation for statewide programs and services provided to the court or courts by the Judicial 

[5:1:58,208] Council or payment for services or property of any kind contracted for by the court or courts or on behalf of the courts by the 

[5:2:58,217] Judicial Council that are paid for or reimbursed by the trial courts. The appropriation also supports the implementation and 

[5:3:58,226] administration of the Civil Representation Pilot Program. 

[5:4:58,244] 0155 - HABEAS CORPUS RESOURCE CENTER 

[6:0:58,262] The Habeas Corpus Resource Center provides legal representation for indigent petitioners in death penalty habeas corpus 

[6:1:58,271] proceedings before the Supreme Court of California and the federal courts. The Center also recruits and trains attorneys to 

[6:2:58,280] expand the pool of private counsel qualified to accept appointments in death penalty habeas corpus proceedings, serves as 

[6:3:58,289] a resource to them, and thereby helps to reduce the number of unrepresented indigents on California's death row.

[11:0:58,502] INFRASTRUCTURE OVERVIEW 

[12:0:58,521] The Judicial Council facilities consist of the offices of its staff, the Supreme Court, the Courts of Appeal, the Habeas Corpus 

[12:1:58,530] Resource Center, the Commission on Judicial Performance, and all Trial Courts statewide. The Supreme Court is located in 

[12:2:58,539] the Civic Center Plaza in San Francisco (98,000 square feet) and the Ronald Reagan State Building in Los Angeles (7,600 

[12:3:58,548] sf). The Courts of Appeal are organized into six districts, operate in nine different locations, and consist of approximately 

[12:4:58,557] 508,000 sf. The Trial Courts are located in 58 counties statewide consisting of more than 500 buildings and 2,100 

[12:5:58,566] courtrooms and approximately 14 million sf of usable area. The space includes public areas, such as courtrooms, waiting 

[12:6:58,575] areas, clerks' offices, child waiting, records viewing, rooms for jury assembly and deliberation, and centers for self-help, 

[12:7:58,584] alternative dispute resolution, and mediation, as well as private areas, such as judicial officer chambers, staff workspace, 

[12:8:58,593] storage space, training rooms, and conference rooms. Judicial Council staff facilities, occupying approximately 255,000 sf, 

[12:9:58,602] are located in San Francisco (Headquarters), Sacramento, and field offices throughout the state. Judicial Council 

[12:10:58,611] responsibility and management has gradually increased to what is now approximately 20 million square feet of facility space 

[12:11:58,620] statewide.

[3:0:178,149] 0280 Commission on Judicial Performance 

[4:0:58,170] The California Commission on Judicial Performance is the independent state agency responsible for investigating 

[4:1:58,179] complaints of judicial misconduct and judicial incapacity, and for disciplining judges pursuant to Article VI, Section 18 of the 

[4:2:58,188] California Constitution. It is the only body with such authority in the state. Its jurisdiction includes all active judges and 

[4:3:58,197] justices of California's superior courts, Courts of Appeal and Supreme Court, and former judges for conduct prior to 

[4:4:58,206] retirement or resignation. The Commission also shares authority with the local courts for the oversight of court 

[4:5:58,215] commissioners and referees. In addition to its disciplinary functions, the Commission is responsible for handling judges' 

[4:6:58,224] applications for disability retirement. 

[5:0:58,242] The Commission's authority is limited to investigating alleged judicial misconduct and, if warranted, imposing discipline. 

[5:1:58,251] Judicial misconduct usually involves conduct in conflict with the standards set forth in the Code of Judicial Ethics. After 

[5:2:58,260] investigation and, in some cases a public hearing, the Commission may impose sanctions ranging from confidential 

[5:3:58,269] discipline to removal from office. 

[6:0:58,287] The Commission is composed of 11 members: 3 judges appointed by the Supreme Court; 2 attorneys appointed by the 

[6:1:58,296] Governor; and 6 lay citizens, of which 2 are appointed by the Governor, 2 are appointed by the Senate Committee on Rules, 

[6:2:58,305] and 2 are appointed by the Speaker of the Assembly. Members are appointed to four-year terms and may serve two terms. 

[6:3:58,314] Commission members do not receive a salary.

[8:0:148,410] 0390 Contributions to the Judges' Retirement System 

[8:1:58,430] The Judges' Retirement System provides retirement benefit funding for judges on California's Supreme, Appellate, and 

[8:2:58,439] Superior/Municipal courts. 

[9:0:58,457] The Judges' Retirement System provides retirement, disability, and death benefits based on age, years of service, 

[9:1:58,466] compensation of active judges, and eligibility, as determined by specific sections of the Judges' Retirement Law. Active 

[9:2:58,475] judges and the state each contribute 8 percent of salary to the Judges' Retirement System. Additional contributions come 

[9:3:58,484] from filing fees for specific civil cases and investment income. These contributions, however, are not sufficient to fully fund 

[9:4:58,493] benefit payments. Consequently, current law requires the state to fund the difference between existing contribution sources 

[9:5:58,502] and the required benefit payments to retired judges. 

[10:0:58,520] A second retirement system for judges was established in 1994. All new judges elected or appointed on or after November 

[10:1:58,529] 9, 1994 become members of the Judges' Retirement System II. The Judges' Retirement System II provides retirement, 

[10:2:58,538] disability, and death benefits based on age, years of service, final compensation, and eligibility, as determined by specific 

[10:3:58,547] sections of the Judges' Retirement System II Law. Members not eligible for a defined benefit receive the balance of their 

[10:4:58,556] monetary credits (in a lump-sum payment). The Judges' Retirement System II receives contributions from judges equal to 8 

[10:5:58,565] percent of salary as well as any investment income. The state's contributions are adjusted annually to maintain actuarial 

[10:6:58,574] soundness of the fund. Judges' Retirement System II members eligible for a service retirement have the option of choosing 

[10:7:58,583] the monetary credit plan (a lump-sum return of contributions and interest earned) or the defined benefit plan. 

[11:0:58,601] Effective January 1, 2013, provisions of the California Public Employees' Pension Reform Act of 2013, Chapter 296, Statutes 

[11:1:58,610] of 2012 (AB 340), require that new judges contribute 50 percent of the normal cost of their pension benefits.

[15:0:58,610] 0220 - GO-Biz 

[16:0:58,628] The GO-Biz serves as the Governor's lead entity for economic strategy and the marketing of California on issues relating to 

[16:1:58,637] business development, private sector investment, and economic growth, and export promotion. This program makes 

[16:2:58,646] recommendations to the Governor and the Legislature regarding policies, programs, and actions to advance statewide 

[16:3:58,655] economic goals. 

[17:0:58,673] 0225 - CALIFORNIA BUSINESS INVESTMENT SERVICES 

[18:0:58,691] This program serves employers, corporate executives, business owners, and site location consultants who are considering 

[18:1:58,700] California for business investment and expansion. This program convenes teams on key business development issues. 

[18:2:58,709] This program works with local, state, and federal partners to attract, retain, and grow businesses in addition to providing 

[18:3:58,718] permit assistance and helping businesses succeed in California. The Innovation Hub (iHub) initiative improves the state's 

[18:4:58,727] national and global competitiveness by stimulating partnerships, economic development, and job creation around specific

[0:0:58,15] 2017-18 STATE BUDGET — LJE 50   LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE

[2:0:58,91] research clusters through state-designated iHubs. 

[2:1:58,109] 0230 - OFFICE OF THE SMALL BUSINESS ADVOCATE 

[3:0:58,127] The director of the Office of the Small Business Advocate (OSBA) serves as the principal advocate in the state on behalf of 

[3:1:58,136] small businesses, including legislation and administrative regulations that affect small business. The OSBA is responsible 

[3:2:58,145] for disseminating information about programs and services provided by the state that benefit small businesses, and how 

[3:3:58,154] small businesses can participate in these programs and services. The OSBA responds to issues from small businesses 

[3:4:58,163] concerning the actions of state agencies, state laws and regulations adversely affecting those businesses. The OSBA 

[3:5:58,172] maintains and distributes an annual list of persons serving as small business ombudsmen throughout state government. 

[3:6:58,190] 0235010 - CALIFORNIA FILM COMMISSION 

[4:0:58,208] The California Film Commission (CFC) enhances California's status as the leader in motion picture, television and 

[4:1:58,217] commercial production. The Commission is tasked with retaining and increasing motion picture production and to see that it 

[4:2:58,226] continues to create jobs and boost business throughout the State. A one-stop office for filmmakers, the Commission 

[4:3:58,235] supports productions of all sizes and budgets with a variety of services. In addition to issuing film permits for all state 

[4:4:58,244] properties, administering the film and TV tax credit program, maintaining an extensive location library, and offering 

[4:5:58,253] production assistance on a wide variety of issues, CFC also works closely with cities and counties with the goal of creating 

[4:6:58,262] 'film friendly" policies that are consistent state-wide. 

[4:7:58,280] 0235019 - DIVISION OF TOURISM 

[5:0:58,298] The California Tourism Market Act provides for the marketing of California through an assessment of businesses that benefit 

[5:1:58,307] from travel and tourism. The objective of the Tourism Assessment Program is to identify potentially assessable businesses, 

[5:2:58,316] assist companies with determining the appropriate amount of their self-assessment, and collet the fee. 

[5:3:58,334] 0235028 - CALIFORINIA INFRASTRUCTURE AND ECONOMIC DEVELOPMENT BANK 

[6:0:58,352] California Infrastructure and Economic Development Bank (IBank) was created to finance public infrastructure and private 

[6:1:58,361] development that promote a healthy climate for jobs, contribute to a strong economy and improve the quality of life in 

[6:2:58,370] California communities. IBank has a broad authority to issue tax-exempt and taxable revenue bonds, provide financing to 

[6:3:58,379] public agencies, provide credit enhancements, acquire or lease facilities, and leverage State and Federal funds. IBank's 

[6:4:58,388] current programs include the infrastructure state revolving fund, 501(c)(3) tax-exempt and taxable revenue bond program, 

[6:5:58,397] industrial development revenue bond program, exempt facility revenue bond program, governmental bond program and the 

[6:6:58,406] Clean Energy Finance Center (CEFC) and the Statewide Energy Efficiency Program under the CEFC. 

[6:7:58,424] 0235037 - SMALL BUSINESS LOAN GUARANTEE PROGRAM 

[7:0:58,442] The Small Business Loan Guarantee Program (SBLGP) promotes local economic development by providing guarantees for 

[7:1:58,451] loans issued to small businesses from financial institutions, typically banks, that otherwise would not approve a term loan or 

[7:2:58,460] line of credit to a small business. As a result of the SBLGP, participating small businesses are able to secure financing that 

[7:3:58,469] allows them to grow and expand their business. The loan guarantee serves as a credit enhancement and an incentive for 

[7:4:58,478] financial institutions to make loans to small businesses that otherwise would not be eligible for such financing. 

[7:5:58,496] 0235046 - CALIFORNIA WELCOME CENTERS 

[8:0:58,514] California Welcome Centers are visitor information centers that are readily accessible to and recognizable by tourists to 

[8:1:58,523] encourage tourism in California and provide benefits to the state economy. The objective of the California Welcome Center 

[8:2:58,532] Program is to determine the locality of underserved travelers, designate a welcome center, and establish operating 

[8:3:58,541] standards across the network.

[7:0:115,346] 0530 Secretary for California Health and Human Services Agency 

[8:0:58,367] The primary mission of the Health and Human Services Agency (HHSA) is to provide policy leadership and direction to the 

[8:1:58,376] departments, board and programs it oversees, to reduce duplication and fragmentation among HHSA departments in policy 

[8:2:58,385] development and implementation, to improve coordination among departments on common programs, to ensure 

[8:3:58,394] programmatic integrity, and to advance the Governor's priorities on health and human services issues. 

[9:0:58,412] The HHSA accomplishes its mission through the administration and coordination of state and federal programs for public 

[9:1:58,421] health, health care services, social services, public assistance, health planning and licensing, and rehabilitation. These 

[10:0:58,430] programs touch the lives of millions of California's most needy and vulnerable residents. The HHSA is committed to striking 

[10:1:58,439] a balance between maintaining access to essential health and human services for California's most disadvantaged and at-

[10:2:58,448] risk residents while pursuing ways to better manage and control costs. 

[11:0:58,466] The following departments and entities fall under the purview of the HHSA:

[12:0:58,232] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[13:0:58,259] 0280 - SECRETARY FOR HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[14:0:58,277] The Secretary for California Health and Human Services Agency provides the Governor with the highest level of advice on 

[14:1:58,286] state health, human services and related budget policy issues. The Secretary also provides the highest level of leadership 

[14:2:58,295] and oversight of the agency-wide efforts to promote the health and well-being of a growing and increasingly diverse 

[14:3:58,304] California population. 

[15:0:58,322] 0285 - THE CALIFORNIA OFFICE OF HEALTH INFORMATION INTEGRITY 

[16:0:58,340] The California Office of Health Information Integrity (CalOHII) is responsible for statewide leadership, coordination, policy 

[16:1:58,349] formation, direction, and oversight responsibilities for federal Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act (HIPAA) 

[16:2:58,358] requirements. As the leading resource for providing HIPAA expertise to the State of California, CalOHII exercises full 

[16:3:58,367] authority relative to state entities to establish policy, provide direction to state entities, monitor progress and report on 

[16:4:58,376] implementation efforts based on state and federal laws. 

[17:0:58,394] 0290 - OFFICE OF SYSTEMS INTEGRATION 

[18:0:58,412] This Office provides project management services for automation projects for the Health and Human Services Agency, the 

[18:1:58,421] Department of Social Services, the Department of Health Care Services, the Department of Public Health, and the Health 

[18:2:58,430] Benefit Exchange, including:

[10:0:162,481] 0540 Secretary of the Natural Resources Agency 

[10:1:58,502] The mission of the Natural Resources Agency is to restore, protect and manage the state's natural, historical and cultural 

[10:2:58,511] resources for current and future generations using creative approaches and solutions based on science, collaboration and 

[10:3:58,520] respect for all involved communities. The secretary for Natural Resources, a member of the Governor's Cabinet, sets the 

[10:4:58,529] policies and coordinates the environmental preservation and restoration activities of 26 various departments, boards, 

[10:5:58,538] commissions and conservancies, and directly administers the Sea Grant Program, Ocean Protection Council, California 

[10:6:58,547] Environmental Quality Act, Environmental Enhancement Mitigation Program, River Parkways, Urban Greening, and the 

[10:7:58,556] California Cultural and Historical Endowment grant programs. 

[11:0:58,574] The Natural Resources Agency consists of the departments of Forestry and Fire Protection, Conservation, Fish and Wildlife, 

[11:1:58,583] Parks and Recreation, and Water Resources; the California Conservation Corps; Exposition Park; California Science Center; 

[11:2:58,592] California African American Museum; the State Lands Commission; the Colorado River Board; the San Francisco Bay 

[11:3:58,601] Conservation and Development Commission; the Energy Resources Conservation and Development Commission; the 

[11:4:58,610] Wildlife Conservation Board; the Delta Protection Commission; the California Coastal Commission; the State Coastal 

[11:5:58,619] Conservancy; the California Tahoe Conservancy; the Santa Monica Mountains Conservancy; the Coachella Valley 

[11:6:58,628] Mountains Conservancy; the San Joaquin River Conservancy; the San Gabriel and Lower Los Angeles Rivers and 

[11:7:58,637] Mountains Conservancy; the Baldwin Hills Conservancy; the San Diego River Conservancy; the Sierra Nevada 

[12:0:58,646] Conservancy; the Sacramento-San Joaquin Delta Conservancy; the Native American Heritage Commission; and the Special 

[12:1:58,655] Resources Program.

[12:0:58,555] MAJOR PROGRAM CHANGES 

[13:0:68,571] • 

[14:0:78,573] The Budget establishes a new Natural Resources and Parks Preservation Fund, which is a "pay as you go" special 

[14:1:78,582] fund to support natural resources programs previously funded by bond measures, such as water and flood 

[14:2:78,591] management, parks, forestry, land preservation, wildlife habitat, and climate adaptation. This new approach will be cost 

[14:3:78,600] effective, as the state will get double the value for each dollar compared to bond financing. The amount of funding 

[14:4:78,609] allocated for this Fund will be determined on a year-to-year basis.

[7:0:198,266] 0552 Office of the Inspector General 

[7:1:58,286] The Office of the Inspector General (OIG) protects public safety by safeguarding the integrity of California's correctional 

[7:2:58,295] system. The OIG is responsible for contemporaneous oversight of the California Department of Corrections and 

[7:3:58,304] Rehabilitation's (CDCR) internal affairs investigations, use of force, and the employee disciplinary process. When requested 

[7:4:58,313] by the Governor, the Senate Committee on Rules, or the Speaker of the Assembly, the Inspector General reviews the 

[7:5:58,322] policies, practices, and procedures of the CDCR. The Inspector General reviews the Governor's candidates for appointment 

[7:6:58,331] to serve as warden for the state's adult correctional institutions and as superintendents for the state's juvenile facilities; 

[7:7:58,340] conducts metric-oriented inspection programs to periodically review delivery of medical care at each state prison and the 

[7:8:58,349] delivery of reforms implemented by the CDCR since 2012. The OIG receives communications from individuals alleging 

[7:9:58,358] improper governmental activity and maintains a toll-free public telephone number to receive allegations of wrongdoing by 

[7:10:58,367] employees of the CDCR; conducts formal reviews of complaints of retaliation from CDCR employees against upper 

[7:11:58,376] management where a legally cognizable cause of action is present; and reviews the mishandling of sexual abuse incidents 

[7:12:58,385] within correctional institutions. The OIG provides critical public transparency for the state correctional system by publicly 

[7:13:58,394] reporting its findings. 

[8:0:58,412] In addition, the OIG is responsible for the California Rehabilitation Oversight Board (Board) that examines CDCR's various 

[8:1:58,421] mental health, substance abuse, educational, and employment programs for inmates and parolees. The Board meets at 

[8:2:58,430] least twice annually to recommend modifications, additions, and eliminations of offender rehabilitation and treatment 

[8:3:58,439] programs. The Board also submits biannual reports to the Governor, the Legislature, and the public to convey its findings on 

[8:4:58,448] the effectiveness of treatment efforts, rehabilitation needs of offenders, gaps in offender rehabilitation services, and levels of 

[8:5:58,457] offender participation and success.

[7:0:174,292] 0555 Secretary for Environmental Protection 

[7:1:58,312] The Secretary for Environmental Protection is the cabinet level agency responsible for protecting human health and the 

[8:0:58,321] environment. California Environmental Protection Agency programs reduce greenhouse gas emissions, restore and protect 

[8:1:58,330] environmental quality, and protect public health. The Secretary coordinates the state's environmental regulatory programs 

[8:2:58,339] and ensures fair and consistent enforcement of environmental law, which safeguards the state's residents and promotes the 

[8:3:58,348] state's economic vitality. The Secretary also administers environmental justice, environmental law enforcement, emergency 

[8:4:58,357] preparedness and response, Certified Unified Program Agencies, and scientific review programs. The Secretary leads 

[9:0:58,366] greenhouse gas emission reduction and climate change activities in state government, and is responsible for coordinating 

[9:1:58,375] the implementation of Chapter 488, Statutes of 2006 (AB 32). The Secretary also centralizes coordination of California-

[9:2:58,384] Mexico border environmental efforts.

[9:0:193,341] 0650 Office of Planning and Research 

[9:1:58,362] The Office of Planning and Research (OPR) assists the Governor and the Administration in planning, research, policy 

[9:2:58,371] development, and legislative analysis. OPR formulates long-range state goals and policies to address land use, climate 

[9:3:58,380] change, population growth and distribution, urban expansion, infrastructure development, groundwater sustainability and 

[9:4:58,389] drought response, and resource protection. OPR also maintains and updates the General Plan Guidelines, the California 

[9:5:58,398] Environmental Quality Act Guidelines, and operates the CEQA Clearinghouse. OPR acts as the state's liaison to a variety of 

[9:6:58,407] entities including local government, planning professionals, small business, and the military. OPR houses and supports the 

[9:7:58,416] Strategic Growth Council. In addition, OPR houses California Volunteers, a program aimed to increase the number and 

[9:8:58,425] impact of Californians involved with service and volunteering throughout the state, and runs the State Clearinghouse, 

[9:9:58,434] coordinating CEQA filings and state compliance issues.

[14:0:58,475] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[15:0:58,503] 0360 - STATE PLANNING AND POLICY DEVELOPMENT 

[16:0:58,521] The major activities of OPR include: (1) recommending and implementing state policies on land-use and growth planning, 

[16:1:58,530] including General Plan Guidelines; (2) coordinating the implementation of the California Environmental Quality Act, 

[16:2:58,539] including: (a) operating the State Clearinghouse; (b) maintaining an online database for the electronic submission and 

[16:3:58,548] archiving of CEQA documents; (c) developing CEQA guidelines; (d) providing technical assistance; (e) streamlining 

[16:4:58,557] permitting; and (f) providing training; (3) supporting the Governor's Advisor for Military Affairs and Governor's Military 

[16:5:58,566] Council; (4) providing policy research for the Governor and Cabinet; (5) providing technical advice to, and develop guidelines 

[16:6:58,575] for, local governments on land use planning and compliance with environmental statutes and regulations; (6) developing a 

[16:7:58,584] program to coordinate regional and local efforts with state climate adaptation strategies on the impacts of climate change ; 

[16:8:58,593] (7) supporting drought response efforts; (8) supporting development of state plans including, but not limited to, the Water 

[16:9:58,602] Action Plan work, State Multi-Hazard Mitigation Plan, Safeguarding California Plan, the Integrated Energy Policy Report, and 

[16:10:58,611] the 5-Year Infrastructure Plan; (9) supporting multiple efforts to address climate change and response to carbon pollution; 

[16:11:58,620] (10) administering the Integrated Climate Adaptation and Resiliency Program to coordinate regional and local efforts with 

[16:12:58,629] state climate adaptation strategies to adapt to the impacts of climate change; (11) serving as the primary point of contact for 

[16:13:58,638] information on federal grants related to community, economic, and local development, as well as the coordinator to manage 

[16:14:58,647] and maximize federal grant opportunities within the state; and (12) conducting other activities as the Governor may direct. 

[16:15:58,665] 0365 - CALIFORNIA VOLUNTEERS

[17:1:58,692] volunteering throughout the state. California Volunteers administers programs such as AmeriCorps and Disaster 

[17:2:58,701] Volunteering and Preparedness, guides policy development to support the nonprofit and service fields, and leads the 

[17:3:58,710] Service Enterprise Initiative, which empowers a nonprofit to more efficiently engage volunteers and effectively address 

[17:4:58,719] community needs. Through the efforts of California Volunteers, Californians of all ages and abilities are provided ongoing 

[17:5:58,728] opportunities to volunteer, to become better prepared to respond in emergencies and disasters, and ultimately, to embrace a

[3:0:58,91] 0370 - STRATEGIC GROWTH COUNCIL 

[4:0:58,109] The Council coordinates interagency efforts and partners with local and regional government stakeholders to promote 

[4:1:58,118] sustainable development, improving air and water quality, protecting natural resources and agricultural lands, and reducing 

[4:2:58,127] greenhouse gas emissions. The Council administers the Transformative Climate Communities Program, the Affordable 

[4:3:58,136] Housing and Sustainable Communities Program and the Sustainable Agricultural Lands Conservation Program, developing 

[4:4:58,145] guidelines, reviewing applications, and providing funding as part of greenhouse gas reduction efforts associated with cap 

[4:5:58,154] and trade funds. The Council also administers a technical assistance program to support all Greenhouse Gas Reduction 

[4:6:58,163] Fund programs to assist in the development of projects that maximize greenhouse gas reductions. The Council is charged 

[4:7:58,172] with review of the California 5-Year Infrastructure plan and with making grants and loans to institutions for planning and 

[4:8:58,181] implementing land uses that achieve the goals of the State's Planning Priorities. The Council also oversees the 

[4:9:58,190] Administration's Health in All Policies program, and sponsors research on infill development, conservation, and other 

[4:10:58,199] planning issues.

[6:0:201,292] 0690 Office of Emergency Services 

[6:1:58,312] The principal objective of the Office of Emergency Services (OES) is to protect lives and property, build capabilities, and 

[6:2:58,321] support our communities for a resilient California. The OES Director serves as both the Governor's Homeland Security 

[6:3:58,330] Advisor and Emergency Management Director, with responsibility to implement and facilitate the state's homeland security 

[6:4:58,339] and counter-terrorism strategy. The OES serves the public through effective collaboration in preparing for, protecting 

[6:5:58,348] against, responding to, recovering from, and mitigating the impacts of all hazards and threats. 

[7:0:58,366] On a day-to-day basis, the OES provides leadership, assistance, training, and support to state and local agencies and 

[7:1:58,375] coordinates with federal agencies in planning and preparing for the most effective use of federal, state, local, and private 

[7:2:58,384] sector resources in emergencies. This emergency planning is based upon a system of mutual aid whereby a jurisdiction 

[7:3:58,393] relies first on its own resources, and then requests assistance from its neighbors. The OES' plans and programs are 

[7:4:58,402] coordinated with those of the federal government, other states, private sector, utilities, and state and local agencies within 

[7:5:58,411] California. 

[8:0:58,429] During an emergency, the OES functions as the Governor's immediate staff to provide guidance and coordinate the state's 

[8:1:58,438] responsibilities under the Emergency Services Act and applicable federal statutes. It also acts as the conduit for federal 

[8:2:58,447] assistance through natural disaster grants and federal agency support. Additionally, the OES is responsible for the 

[9:0:58,456] development and coordination of a comprehensive state strategy related to all hazards, including terrorism, which includes 

[9:1:58,465] prevention, preparedness, mitigation, response, and recovery. 

[10:0:58,483] The OES implements the state homeland security strategy by overseeing the State Threat Assessment System (STAS), 

[10:1:58,492] which includes management of the State Threat Assessment Center (STAC). The STAS is comprised of four regional and 

[10:2:58,501] one major urban area Fusion Centers that assist in the detection, prevention, investigation, and response to criminal and 

[10:3:58,510] terrorist activity; and information and intelligence sharing between local, state, federal, tribal agencies, and private sector 

[10:4:58,519] partners. The STAC operates as the state's information-sharing clearinghouse for strategic threat analysis, counter-

[10:5:58,528] terrorism, situational awareness reporting, and case analysis for statewide leadership, agencies, and public safety 

[10:6:58,537] community. Further, the OES improves the criminal justice system in California by providing financial and technical 

[10:7:58,546] assistance to local governments, state agencies, and the private sector for homeland security, public safety, and victim 

[10:8:58,555] services. 

[11:0:58,573] Because the OES' programs drive a need for infrastructure investment, the department has a capital outlay program to 

[11:1:58,582] support this need. For the specifics on the department's capital outlay program see "Infrastructure Overview."

[0:0:58,15] 2017-18 STATE BUDGET — LJE 102   LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE 

[1:0:166,44] 0690 Office of Emergency Services - Continued 

[2:0:58,82] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[3:0:58,109] 0380 - EMERGENCY MANAGEMENT SERVICES 

[4:0:58,127] Through the Emergency Management Services and Homeland Security Program, the OES provides effective use of federal, 

[4:1:58,136] state, and local resources, through the mutual aid system to jurisdictions whose resources and services are overextended in 

[4:2:58,145] a disaster situation. Also, this program develops and coordinates a comprehensive state strategy related to an all-hazards 

[4:3:58,154] approach that includes prevention, preparedness, mitigation, response, and recovery consistent with the National Strategy 

[4:4:58,163] on Homeland Security. Central to this effort is maintaining operational readiness at all levels of government. Within this 

[4:5:58,172] program, the OES also trains emergency managers, responders, and state and local leaders in preparedness and response 

[4:6:58,181] to all hazards. 

[5:0:58,199] 0385 - SPECIAL PROGRAMS AND GRANT MANAGEMENT 

[6:0:58,217] The OES serves as the State Administering Agent for federal homeland security, emergency management, and victim 

[6:1:58,226] services grants and is the primary liaison with the Federal Emergency Management Agency, the United States Department 

[6:2:58,235] of Homeland Security, and other federal agencies. Additionally, the OES serves as an advocate for local public safety, 

[6:3:58,244] emergency management, and public and private agencies operating public safety and victim service programs. As part of its 

[6:4:58,253] grant management role, the OES administers the California Disaster Assistance Act and provides eligible local agencies with 

[6:5:58,262] financial assistance to recover from disasters. Included in this program is the State Threat Assessment Center which is the 

[6:6:58,271] centerpiece of the State's intelligence information sharing environment and serves as the Governor's designated primary 

[6:7:58,280] fusion center. 

[7:0:58,298] 0395 - PUBLIC SAFETY COMMUNICATIONS 

[8:0:58,316] Public Safety Communications (PSC) serves the State of California by providing public safety communications to the State's 

[8:1:58,325] first responders and oversight of the 9-1-1 system to the people of California. The PSC is dedicated to the preservation and 

[8:2:58,334] protection of human life and public safety by delivering reliable and dependable communication services keeping the public 

[8:3:58,343] connected during times of crisis. 

[8:4:58,361] 9900 - ADMINISTRATION AND EXECUTIVE 

[9:0:58,379] The Administration and Executive Program provides the overall policy direction of the OES and support services such as 

[9:1:58,388] accounting, fiscal, personnel, information technology, and business services.

[2:0:58,89] INFRASTRUCTURE OVERVIEW 

[3:0:58,108] The Office of Emergency Services' infrastructure includes a headquarters facility, an administrative building, and an Inland 

[3:1:58,117] Regional Operations Center in Sacramento County; a Coastal Regional Operations Center in Walnut Creek, Contra Costa 

[3:2:58,126] County; a Southern Regional Operations Center located at Los Alamitos Joint Forces Training Base in Orange County; the 

[3:3:58,135] California Specialized Training Institute at Camp San Luis Obispo; and various small field offices throughout the state. 

[3:4:58,153] The Public Safety Communications division (PSC) is comprised of a main leased complex in Sacramento and 45 field 

[3:5:58,162] locations throughout the state. These locations include 8 area offices and 37 area shops, positioned geographically to 

[3:6:58,171] facilitate maintenance and installation services to remote communication sites and customers throughout the state. In 

[3:7:58,180] addition, the PSC maintains and operates 10 communications vaults/towers and a total of more than 3,500 radio frequency 

[3:8:58,189] points of presence.

[0:0:58,15] LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE   2017-18 STATE BUDGET — LJE 117 

[1:0:190,44] 0750 Office of the Lieutenant Governor 

[1:1:58,64] Under California's Constitution, the Lieutenant Governor serves as Acting Governor whenever the Governor is absent from 

[1:2:58,73] the state, and automatically becomes Governor if a vacancy occurs in the Office of Governor. The Lieutenant Governor is 

[1:3:58,82] also President of the Senate and votes in case of a tie. 

[2:0:58,100] The Lieutenant Governor serves as a voting member of the Board of Regents of the University of California and a voting 

[2:1:58,109] member of the Board of Trustees of the California State University system. 

[3:0:58,127] The Lieutenant Governor also serves on, and rotates with the State Controller, as chair of the three-member State Lands 

[3:1:58,136] Commission, which oversees the control and leasing of millions of acres of state-owned land, including offshore oil 

[3:2:58,145] resources, as well as use and permitting for all navigable waterways in California. The Commission also manages state 

[3:3:58,154] land-use planning and revenues, and related interstate issues. During alternate years, when the Lieutenant Governor 

[3:4:58,163] serves as Chairperson of the State Lands Commission, he also serves as a member of the Ocean Protection Council. 

[3:5:58,181] In addition, under state statutes, the Lieutenant Governor chairs the California Commission for Economic Development, 

[3:6:58,190] which provides support and guidance to the Governor, Legislature and private sector regarding the development of 

[3:7:58,199] California's economy.

[18:0:58,322] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[19:0:58,350] 0435 - LEGAL SERVICES 

[20:0:58,368] Legal Services is organized into three elements: (1) Civil Law, (2) Criminal Law, and (3) Public Rights. 

[21:0:58,386] Civil Law represents the State of California and its officers, agencies, departments, boards, commissions, and employees in 

[21:1:58,395] civil matters. It provides advice to these clients, defends cases brought against them and prosecutes cases to vindicate state 

[21:2:58,404] interests. Deputy Attorneys General in Civil Law are responsible for managing and litigating cases before administrative 

[21:3:58,413] tribunals, and in both state and federal courts at the trial level and on appeal, including appeals before the United States and 

[21:4:58,422] California Supreme Courts. Deputies work in one of eight sections: Business and Tax; Correctional Law; Employment and 

[21:5:58,431] Administrative Mandates; Government Law; Health, Education and Welfare; Health Quality Enforcement; Licensing; or Tort 

[21:6:58,440] and Condemnation. 

[22:0:58,458] Criminal Law represents the state in criminal matters before the Appellate and Supreme courts. Criminal Law also fulfills the 

[22:1:58,467] Attorney General's responsibilities of assisting district attorneys in cases for which they are recused, conducts criminal 

[22:2:58,476] investigations, represents the Governor, Board of Parole Hearings, and California Department of Corrections and 

[22:3:58,485] Rehabilitation in state and federal habeas corpus cases and appeals, and other proceedings relating to parole decisions and 

[22:4:58,494] conditions of confinement in the state prisons and defends state and federal habeas corpus matters. Additional 

[22:5:58,503] responsibilities include enforcing the Political Reform Act, advising the Governor on extradition matters, investigating and 

[22:6:58,512] prosecuting Medi-Cal provider fraud, investigating and prosecuting the abuse or neglect of elder and dependent adults 

[22:7:58,521] residing in long-term health care facilities, and investigating, prosecuting, and coordinating litigation involving white-collar 

[22:8:58,530] crime, high-tech/computer/privacy crime, financial crimes against the elderly, human trafficking, environmental crimes, and 

[22:9:58,539] public corruption. 

[23:0:58,557] Public Rights protects and preserves the public interest by providing legal services to state agencies and Constitutional 

[23:1:58,566] Officers and by bringing actions in the name of the Attorney General to protect the public. Public Rights provides specialized 

[23:2:58,575] services in the following areas: Civil Rights Enforcement (including Underground Economy and the Bureau of Children's 

[23:3:58,584] Justice); Charitable Trusts (including the Registry of Charitable Trusts); Natural Resources Law; Corporate Fraud (including 

[23:4:58,593] False Claims, Energy and Corporate Responsibility); Indian and Gaming Law; Environment Law; Land Law; Consumer Law 

[23:5:58,602] (including Sellers of Travel and Privacy Enforcement and Protection); Antitrust Law; and Tobacco Litigation Enforcement. 

[24:0:58,620] 0440 - LAW ENFORCEMENT 

[25:0:58,638] The Division of Law Enforcement is organized into five elements: (1) Bureau of Firearms, (2) Bureau of Forensic Services, 

[25:1:58,647] (3) Bureau of Gambling Control, (4) Bureau of Investigation, and (5) the Office of the Director. 

[26:0:58,665] The Bureau of Firearms provides oversight, enforcement, education, and regulation of California's firearms/dangerous 

[26:1:58,674] weapon laws by conducting firearms eligibility background checks and administering over thirty different state-mandated 

[26:2:58,683] firearms-related programs. The Bureau conducts firearms dealer and manufacturer inspections and provides training as 

[26:3:58,692] needed. Special Agents conduct investigations on armed and prohibited persons and other investigations resulting in the 

[26:4:58,701] seizure of weapons. Agents also conduct firearms investigations to prevent illegal gun trafficking at in-state and out-of-state 

[26:5:58,710] gun shows in accordance with state and federal law. 

[27:0:58,728] The Bureau of Forensic Services (BFS) provides evaluation and analysis of physical evidence, including crime scene 

[28:0:58,745] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details. 


# === PAGE 124 === [size: 612x792]
[0:0:58,15] 2017-18 STATE BUDGET — LJE 122   LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE 

[1:0:187,44] 0820 Department of Justice - Continued 

[2:0:58,73] investigation and expert court testimony to federal, state and local law enforcement agencies, district attorneys, and courts, 

[2:1:58,82] by operating 11 specialized laboratories that serve 46 counties as well as a forensic training facility. BFS maintains the state 

[2:2:58,91] DNA laboratory database which compiles DNA profiles of sex and violent offenders and felony arrestees. 

[3:0:58,109] The Bureau of Gambling Control regulates legal gambling activities in California to ensure gambling is conducted honestly 

[3:1:58,118] and is free from criminal and corruptive elements. This is accomplished by investigating the qualifications of individuals and 

[3:2:58,127] business entities who apply for state gambling licenses and monitoring the conduct of these licensees to ensure compliance 

[3:3:58,136] with the Gambling Control Act. Furthermore, the Bureau conducts criminal investigations in, on or about Tribal casinos and 

[3:4:58,145] California cardrooms. The Bureau also regulates Tribal gaming to ensure that each Tribe is in compliance with all aspects of 

[3:5:58,154] the negotiated gaming compact. 

[4:0:58,172] The Bureau of Investigation is the premiere investigative agency that is responsible for exploiting and dismantling criminal 

[4:1:58,181] organizations, as well as assisting with the prosecution of serious criminal offenses which present a significant and multi-

[4:2:58,190] jurisdictional threat to California. The Bureau prioritizes investigations related to transnational criminal organizations involved 

[4:3:58,199] in gangs and human trafficking, as well as cases involving environmental crimes, public corruption, major fraud, 

[5:0:58,208] underground economy, and high-technology crimes. In addition, the Bureau serves a principal role in providing leadership, 

[5:1:58,217] coordination, and support to law enforcement through multi-agency drug, gang and major crimes task forces statewide. 

[6:0:58,235] The Office of the Director enhances public safety by providing training, technical, and administrative support to the 

[7:0:58,244] investigative, regulatory and forensic components of the Division of Law Enforcement and other criminal justice agencies. 

[7:1:58,253] The Office serves as the policy-making and oversight body for its four operational bureaus. 

[8:0:58,271] 0445 - CALIFORNIA JUSTICE INFORMATION SERVICES 

[9:0:58,289] The California Justice Information Services Division provides criminal justice intelligence, information, and identification 

[9:1:58,298] services to law enforcement, regulatory agencies, and the public. Four major functional areas carry out these primary 

[9:2:58,307] services: 1) The Bureau of Criminal Identification & Investigative Services consolidates the identification, investigative, and 

[9:3:58,316] field services functions, providing information and technical assistance on manual and automated systems including the 

[9:4:58,325] fingerprint identification system and the violent crime information system; 2) The Bureau of Criminal Information and 

[10:0:58,334] Analysis consolidates the functions related to the authorization, release, and use of criminal offender record information for 

[10:1:58,343] law enforcement investigatory and regulatory purposes; 3) The Hawkins Data Center operates the Criminal Justice 

[10:2:58,352] Information System and the California Law Enforcement Telecommunications System; and 4) the Operations Support 

[10:3:58,361] Program provides business resumption planning and administrative support and oversight. 

[11:0:58,379] 9900 - DIRECTORATE AND ADMINISTRATION 

[12:0:58,397] The Directorate and the Administration Division of the Department of Justice consists of the Division of Administrative 

[13:0:58,406] Support and the Attorney General's Executive Office. The executive office maintains overall direction and administration over 

[13:1:58,415] the diverse programs and projects of the department, including the Equal Employment Rights and Resolution Office, the

[8:0:240,254] 0840 State Controller 

[8:1:58,274] The State Controller is the Chief Fiscal Officer of California, the sixth largest economy in the world. Principally responsible 

[8:2:58,283] for transparency and accountability of the state's financial resources, the Controller ensures the appropriate disbursement 

[8:3:58,292] and tracking of taxpayer dollars. The Controller serves on dozens of state boards, commissions, and committees with duties 

[8:4:58,301] ranging from administrative oversight of the nation's two largest public pension funds, to protection of state lands and 

[8:5:58,310] coastlines, to modernization and financing of major infrastructure. The Controller also offers fiscal guidance to local 

[9:0:58,319] governments and has independent auditing authority over government agencies related to the spending of state funds. The 

[9:1:58,328] Controller's primary objectives are to: 

[10:0:58,344] •

[10:7:58,416] • 

[11:0:68,346] Account for and control disbursement of all state funds, issuing warrants in payment of the state's bills, including lottery 

[11:1:68,355] prizes. 

[12:0:68,364] Determine legality and accuracy of financial claims against the state. 

[12:1:68,373] Audit state and local government programs. 

[13:0:68,382] Safeguard many types of assets until claimed by the rightful owners, in accordance with the Unclaimed Property Law. 

[13:1:68,391] Inform the public of the state's financial condition. 

[14:0:68,400] Inform the public of financial transactions of city, county, and other local governments. 

[14:1:68,409] Administer the Uniform State Payroll System. 

[15:0:68,418] Audit and process all personnel and payroll transactions for state civil service, state exempt employees, state university 

[15:1:68,427] employees, and college system employees.

[17:0:58,300] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[18:0:58,327] 0500100 - ACCOUNTING AND REPORTING 

[19:0:58,345] The State Accounting and Reporting Division maintains uniform and systematic control accounts of all receipts, payments, 

[19:1:58,354] state fund balances, and bonded indebtedness; reports the financial condition of the state; monitors the cash flow of the 

[19:2:58,363] General Fund; administers the statewide discharge from accountability program; participates in offsetting monies owed to 

[19:3:58,372] the state; and collaborates with the Department of Finance, the Treasurer, and the Department of General Services to 

[19:4:58,381] develop and implement the Financial Information System for California (FI$Cal) to ensure the system meets the state's 

[19:5:58,390] primary objectives and provides best business practices for the state. 

[20:0:58,408] The Local Government Programs and Services Division maintains a database of information and reports on local financial 

[20:1:58,417] transactions and government compensation; apportions shared revenues to local governments; administers local mandated 

[20:2:58,426] cost programs; approves county cost allocation plans; prescribes uniform accounting procedures for presentation of financial 

[20:3:58,435] data for local governments and trial court revenues; administers and collects estate and inheritance taxes; collects 

[20:4:58,444] delinquent insurance and motor vehicle fuel taxes and petroleum and gas assessments; refunds gasoline taxes paid on fuel 

[20:5:58,453] consumed for off-highway purposes; instructs and advises county tax collectors; and administers the Property Tax 

[20:6:58,462] Postponement Program for senior and disabled citizens.  

[21:0:58,480] 0500200 - AUDITS 

[22:0:58,498] The Audits Division determines the legality and accuracy of all claims against the state through the performance of 

[22:1:58,507] prepayment audits; assures the accuracy of local government claims and financial statements submitted to the state and 

[22:2:58,516] federal governments by establishing and updating audit guidelines, and reviewing audits performed by independent auditors; 

[22:3:58,525] performs field audits for a variety of state and federal programs; reviews the single audits reports of local governments and 

[22:4:58,534] local education agencies that receive "pass-through federal funds" from state agencies; and audits major businesses for 

[22:5:58,543] compliance with the Unclaimed Property Law. 

[23:0:58,561] 0500300 - PERSONNEL/PAYROLL SERVICES 

[24:0:58,579] The Personnel/Payroll Services Division administers the state's payroll, employment history, the automated travel expense 

[24:1:58,588] reimbursement system, and leave accounting processes in a manner that provides accurate, timely and efficient processing 

[24:2:58,597] for the users of these systems. The Division works with other entities, e.g., Department of Human Resources, Judicial 

[24:3:58,606] Council, Department of Finance, and California State University Chancellor's Office, to maximize the efficiency of the state's 

[24:4:58,615] personnel and payroll functions, while continuing to maintain the highest level and quality of customer service. 

[25:0:58,633] The 21st Century Project was initiated to replace existing statewide human resource management systems with a fully 

[25:1:58,642] integrated solution; however, the project was suspended in February 2013, after an unsuccessful eight-month pilot program, 

[25:2:58,651] and terminated in June 2016, after reaching a settlement with the system integrator. The SCO will assess current 

[25:3:58,660] information technology alternatives and the latest industry standards to analyze alternatives through the California 

[25:4:58,669] Department of Technology Project Approval Lifecycle process. 

[26:0:58,687] 0500400 - UNCLAIMED PROPERTY 

[27:0:58,705] The Unclaimed Property Division administers the Unclaimed Property Law by providing one central source for owners to 

[27:1:58,714] claim their property; notifying owners of their unclaimed property before it is transferred to the state; receiving unclaimed 

[27:2:58,723] property from banks, savings and loans, and other business firms; and providing outreach and education for California 

[28:0:58,745] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[2:1:58,91] 0500500 - DISBURSEMENTS 

[3:0:58,109] The Disbursements Bureau provides services to all state Agencies, Departments and Boards. The primary responsibility is 

[3:1:58,118] to produce and deliver all payments of the state's obligations after auditing and clearance through control accounts, including 

[3:2:58,127] personal income tax refunds, payroll, and retirement payments. Disbursements also provides post issuance services, 

[3:3:58,136] including, but not limited to disposition of undeliverable warrants; lost warrant duplication; and maintenance and production 

[3:4:58,145] of paid warrant images. 

[3:5:58,163] 9900100 - ADMINISTRATION

[4:2:58,199] mainframe, client-server and web-based systems; and oversees the planning, procurement, use, and maintenance of 

[4:3:58,208] information technology hardware and software.

[6:0:215,309] 0845 Department of Insurance 

[6:1:58,329] California's publicly-elected Insurance Commissioner regulates the sixth largest insurance economy in the world with 

[6:2:58,338] insurers collecting more than $288 billion in premium annually in California while protecting consumers and the integrity, 

[6:3:58,347] health and vitality of the insurance marketplace. The vision of the California Department of Insurance (CDI) is "Insurance 

[6:4:58,356] Protection for All Californians." CDI accomplishes this by enforcing insurance laws and regulations, assisting consumers in 

[6:5:58,365] their dealings with insurers, and using innovation to improve services for insurance producers and consumers. 

[6:6:58,383] The CDI licenses and regulates insurance companies, and individuals in California. Currently, the CDI oversees and 

[6:7:58,392] licenses approximately 1,300 insurance companies and more than 400,000 individuals and business entities as insurance 

[6:8:58,401] agents, brokers, adjusters and bail agents. Additionally, the CDI receives and investigates approximately 200,000 consumer 

[6:9:58,410] inquiries and complaints annually; performs examinations to ensure the financial solvency of companies; receives more than 

[6:10:58,419] 30,000 suspected fraudulent claim referrals annually; receives and reviews approximately 7,250 rate filing applications 

[6:11:58,428] annually; and works in conjunction with local, state and federal law enforcement agencies to investigate and prosecute 

[6:12:58,437] fraudulent insurance practices.

[0:0:58,15] 2017-18 STATE BUDGET — LJE 162   LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE 

[1:0:180,44] 0845 Department of Insurance - Continued 

[2:0:58,82] The objectives of this program are to: (1) prevent losses to policyholders, beneficiaries or the public due to the insolvency of 

[2:1:58,91] insurers; (2) prevent unlawful or unfair practices by insurers as defined by the Insurance Code; (3) ensure that property and 

[2:2:58,100] casualty insurance rates are not excessive, inadequate, unfairly discriminatory or otherwise in violation of the Insurance 

[2:3:58,109] Code and the California Code of Regulations; (4) review health insurance rates filed with CDI to determine whether they are 

[2:4:58,118] reasonable and attempt to get unreasonable rates lowered by insurers; and (5) ensure that applicants for insurance licenses, 

[2:5:58,127] and holders of insurance licenses, satisfy and maintain the qualifications for licensure. Through the Conservation and 

[2:6:58,136] Liquidation Office, the CDI administers the estates of insolvent and delinquent insurance companies. 

[2:7:58,154] 0525 - CONSUMER PROTECTION 

[3:0:58,172] The objectives of this program are to: (1) provide direct service to California consumers by protecting insurance 

[3:1:58,181] policyholders and other parties involved in insurance transactions against unfair or illegal practices with respect to claims 

[3:2:58,190] handling, rating or underwriting by insurers and (2) protect applicants and policyholders from discriminatory, unlawful or 

[3:3:58,199] fraudulent practices or incompetence relating to the sale of insurance. 

[3:4:58,217] 0530 - FRAUD CONTROL 

[4:0:58,235] The objective of this program is to protect the public from economic loss by actively investigating, arresting and referring for 

[4:1:58,244] prosecution or adjudication those who commit insurance fraud and other violations of the law. The program is primarily 

[4:2:58,253] staffed by sworn peace officers who conduct criminal investigations of insurance fraud and related criminal cases. The 

[4:3:58,262] program also implements the Insurance Frauds Prevention Act, which authorizes the Commissioner to initiate or intervene in 

[4:4:58,271] whistle-blower "qui tam" actions seeking civil penalties against perpetrators of insurance fraud. 

[4:5:58,289] 0535 - GENERAL FUND TAX COLLECTION AND COMPLIANCE 

[5:0:58,307] This program performs tax collection; ensures compliance from insurance companies and surplus line brokers with the laws 

[5:1:58,316] contained in the Insurance Code and Revenue and Taxation Code; and works with the Board of Equalization and State 

[5:2:58,325] Controller's Office with various refund, assessment, and accounting matters relative to the premium tax program. Tax 

[5:3:58,334] collections from this program are deposited in the state's General Fund. 

[5:4:58,352] 9900 - ADMINISTRATION 

[6:0:58,370] This program provides administrative support services to the CDI including budgets, accounting, human resources, business 

[6:1:58,379] services and information technology, as well as legislative and legal services. 

[7:0:58,406] DETAILED EXPENDITURES BY PROGRAM  

[8:0:381,416] 2015-16*   2016-17*   2017-18* 

[8:1:96,430] PROGRAM REQUIREMENTS

[0:0:58,15] LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE   2017-18 STATE BUDGET — LJE 169 

[1:0:182,44] 0850 California State Lottery Commission 

[2:0:58,64] In 1984, Proposition 37 amended the California Constitution to authorize the establishment of a statewide lottery. As an 

[2:1:58,73] initiative statute, the California State Lottery Act (Act) of 1984 created the California State Lottery Commission and gave it 

[2:2:58,82] broad powers to oversee the operations of a statewide lottery. The purpose of the Act was to provide supplemental monies 

[2:3:58,91] to benefit public education. The Lottery is overseen by a five-person Commission appointed by the Governor and confirmed 

[2:4:58,100] by the State Senate. 

[3:0:58,118] The Act initially required that 50 percent of total annual revenues be returned to the public in the form of prizes and at least 

[3:1:58,127] 34 percent of total revenues be allocated to the benefit of public education. No more than 16 percent of total revenues were 

[3:2:58,136] to be used for administrative costs. 

[4:0:58,154] In 2010, the Act was changed to allow the Lottery flexibility to pay out more money in prizes and reduce the administrative 

[4:1:58,163] cost limit to 13 percent of total revenues. Along with that flexibility, the new law requires the Lottery to meet minimum levels 

[4:2:58,172] of contribution to public education. Revenues to education are placed in a special fund, known as the California State Lottery 

[4:3:58,181] Education Fund, which holds revenues until they are allocated on a per capita basis, using prior year certified Average Daily 

[4:4:58,190] Attendance data, to the following categories: K-12 education, Community Colleges, the California State University, the 

[4:5:58,199] University of California, and other educational entities, including the California Schools for the Deaf and Blind. 

[5:0:58,217] In the 31 years since sales began in October 1985 through June 30, 2016, the California State Lottery has raised nearly $31 

[5:1:58,226] billion for public education, including $1.59 billion in FY 2015-16. 

[6:0:58,244] Because of the inherently variable nature of lottery ticket sales, revenue estimates for 2016-17 and 2017-18 cannot be made 

[6:1:58,253] with certainty. 

[7:0:58,280] LEGAL CITATIONS AND AUTHORITY 

[8:0:58,298] DEPARTMENT AUTHORITY 

[9:0:58,316] Government Code, Title 2, Division 1, Chapter 12.5 (Sections 8880-8880.72). 

[10:0:58,745] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[1:0:168,44] 0855 California Gambling Control Commission 

[1:1:58,64] The mission of the California Gambling Control Commission (Commission) is to ensure integrity in California's gaming 

[1:2:58,73] environment. The Commission has jurisdiction over gambling establishments (cardrooms), third-party providers of 

[1:3:58,82] proposition player services, and certain aspects of Tribal casinos, pursuant to its authority under state law and Tribal-State 

[1:4:58,91] Gaming Compacts (Compacts). The Commission also has jurisdiction over gaming policies, regulations, criteria, and 

[1:5:58,100] standards. 

[2:0:58,118] There are 89 licensed cardrooms in California over which the Commission has broad regulatory and adjudicatory authority. 

[2:1:58,127] This authority extends to the operation, concentration, and supervision of the cardrooms and all persons and things related 

[2:2:58,136] to each licensed establishment. 

[3:0:58,154] The Commission has fiduciary, regulatory, and administrative responsibilities related to Tribal gaming that include: (1) 

[3:1:58,163] distributing Tribal gaming revenues to Non-Compact, Non-Gaming and Limited-Gaming Tribes; (2) making suitability 

[3:2:58,172] determinations for key employees, vendors, and financial sources; and (3) serving as the administrator of the Indian Gaming 

[3:3:58,181] Revenue Sharing Trust Fund, Indian Gaming Special Distribution Fund, and the Tribal Nation Grant Fund.

[4:0:207,133] 0860 State Board of Equalization 

[4:1:58,153] Prior to July 1, 2017, the State Board of Equalization (BOE) administered various tax and fee programs including the Sales 

[4:2:58,162] and Use tax, adopted rules and regulations to clarify tax laws, acted as an appellate body for the review of property, 

[4:3:58,171] business and income tax assessments, assessed and allocated the property values of railroads and specified utilities and 

[4:4:58,180] businesses, and oversaw the property tax assessment practices of all 58 county assessors. 

[5:0:58,198] Effective July 1, 2017, legislation enacted as part of the 2017 Budget Act recast the BOE as the California Department of 

[5:1:58,207] Tax and Fee Administration (CDTFA). The CDTFA will perform those statutory duties formerly assigned to the BOE, except 

[5:2:58,216] for tax appeals. The BOE will continue in existence, but will handle only those duties assigned to it by the California 

[5:3:58,225] Constitution, namely the assessment and allocation of the property values of railroads and specified utilities and businesses, 

[5:4:58,234] and the oversight of the property tax assessment practices of all 58 county assessors.
