[3:0:58,125] MAJOR PROGRAM CHANGES 

[4:0:58,141] • 

[5:0:68,144] Legislation enacted concurrent with the 2017 Budget Act recast the State Board of Equalization (BOE) as the California 

[5:1:68,153] Department of Tax and Fee Administration (CDTFA) effective July 1, 2017. The CDTFA will have a Director appointed by 

[5:2:68,162] the Governor, and it will operate under the Government Operations Agency. The CDTFA will perform those statutory 

[5:3:68,171] duties previously performed by the BOE, other than tax appeals, which will be assigned to the newly created Office of Tax 

[5:4:68,180] Appeals effective January 1, 2018. The BOE will remain in existence, but it will be responsible only for those duties 

[5:5:68,189] assigned to it by the California Constitution. The BOE will house the Board Members and their staff, together with those 

[5:6:68,198] current BOE civil service employees who work in those programs still under the BOE's jurisdiction. All other BOE civil 

[5:7:68,207] service employees will transition to the CDTFA. Both the CDTFA and the BOE will be funded in 2017-18 from the 

[5:8:68,216] appropriations provided by the 0860 Budget Unit.

[0:0:58,15] LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE   2017-18 STATE BUDGET — LJE 181 

[1:0:172,44] 0860 State Board of Equalization - Continued 

[2:0:58,73] through this program oversees the 58 County Assessors to validate property tax assessments conform with state law. 

[3:0:58,91] 0570050 - STATE-ASSESSED PROPERTY PROGRAM 

[4:0:58,109] This program is responsible for valuing and assessing inter-county pipelines and properties owned or used by railroads, 

[4:1:58,118] regulated telephone companies, companies transmitting or selling gas or electricity, and private railroad car companies. 

[4:2:58,127] Local jurisdictions use the established values for the levy and collection of local property taxes. In addition, the program 

[4:3:58,136] values and assesses private rail cars and collects the Private Rail Car Tax, which is deposited in the General Fund. 

[5:0:58,154] 0570075 - TIMBER TAX PROGRAM 

[6:0:58,172] This program administers the timber yield tax by establishing the harvest value of timber and collecting a tax on the 

[6:1:58,181] harvested timber. 

[7:0:58,199] 0570100 - SALES AND USE TAX PROGRAM 

[8:0:58,217] This program ensures that all sales and use tax revenues are collected in an equitable and effective manner through 

[8:1:58,226] accurate reporting of tax liability. This is accomplished by detecting and correcting errors in self-assessments, and promptly 

[8:2:58,235] collecting amounts determined to be due and economically recoverable. Under this program, the BOE administers the 

[8:3:58,244] following taxes: State Sales and Use Tax, Bradley-Burns Uniform Local Sales and Use Tax, and District Transactions and 

[8:4:58,253] Use Tax (cities/counties). 

[9:0:58,271] 0570125 - HAZARDOUS SUBSTANCES TAX PROGRAM 

[10:0:58,289] These programs provide revenue for the Hazardous Waste Control Account (HWCA) and the Toxic Substances Control 

[10:1:58,298] Account (TSCA). The fees provide funding to the Department of Toxic Substances to regulate hazardous waste in California. 

[10:2:58,307] Generators of hazardous waste, hazardous waste facilities and certain business organizations, as identified by statutes, are 

[10:3:58,316] subject to the fees. The BOE administers the following fee programs in partnership with the department: Disposal Fee 

[10:4:58,325] (HWCA), Facility Fee (HWCA), Generator Fee (HWCA), Transportable Treatment Unit Fee (HWCA), Activity Fee (HWCA), 

[10:5:58,334] and Environmental Fee (TSCA). 

[11:0:58,352] 0570150 - ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGE TAX PROGRAM 

[12:0:58,370] This program collects the excise tax imposed on the sale, distribution, or importation of alcoholic beverages in California. 

[13:0:58,388] 0570175 - TIRE RECYCLING FEE PROGRAM 

[14:0:58,406] This program provides revenue for the California Tire Recycling Account in the California Tire Recycling Management Fund 

[14:1:58,415] and Air Pollution Control Fund. The fee provides funding to reduce: air pollution, landfill disposal, and stockpiling of used 

[14:2:58,424] tires. The BOE administers the program in partnership with the California Department of Resources Recycling and Recovery 

[14:3:58,433] (CalRecycle) and the Air Resources Board. 

[15:0:58,451] 0570200 - CIGARETTE AND TOBACCO PRODUCTS TAX PROGRAM 

[16:0:58,469] This program provides revenue for the Cigarette Tax Fund, Cigarette and Tobacco Products Surtax Fund, the Breast Cancer 

[16:1:58,478] Fund, and the California Children and Families First Trust Fund. The program objective is to ensure that all cigarette and 

[16:2:58,487] tobacco products tax revenues are collected equitably and effectively by ensuring timely reporting and payment of tax 

[16:3:58,496] liabilities, detecting and correcting errors in reporting, and promptly collecting amounts determined to be due and 

[16:4:58,505] economically recoverable. 

[17:0:58,523] 0570225 - CIGARETTE AND TOBACCO PRODUCTS LICENSING PROGRAM 

[18:0:58,541] This program provides revenue for the Cigarette and Tobacco Products Compliance Fund, which is used to implement, 

[18:1:58,550] enforce, and administer the provisions of the California Cigarette and Tobacco Licensing Act. The purpose of the Act is to 

[18:2:58,559] reduce tax evasion, smuggling, and counterfeiting of cigarette and tobacco products and stamps. It requires statewide 

[18:3:58,568] licensing of all distributors, wholesalers, importers, manufacturers, and retailers of cigarette and tobacco products. 

[19:0:58,586] 0570250 - TRANSPORTATION FUND TAX PROGRAM 

[20:0:58,604] This program provides revenue for the Transportation Tax Fund. Allocations are made from the fund to the Aeronautics 

[20:1:58,613] Account, Harbors and Watercraft Revolving Fund, Off-Highway Vehicle Trust Fund, Highway Users Tax Fund, and 

[20:2:58,622] Department of Food and Agriculture Fund. The objective of this program is to ensure that the motor vehicle fuel, jet fuel, 

[20:3:58,631] various use fuel, and diesel fuel taxes are administered equitably and effectively. Pursuant to the International Fuel Tax 

[20:4:58,640] Agreement (IFTA), the BOE registers interstate truckers whose base state is California. Revenues from this program are 

[20:5:58,649] used to construct and maintain public roads and mass transit systems, airports and waterways. 

[21:0:58,667] 0570275 - OCCUPATIONAL LEAD POISONING PREVENTION FEE PROGRAM 

[22:0:58,685] This program provides revenue for the Occupational Lead Poisoning Prevention Account in the General Fund. The funds are 

[22:1:58,694] used to establish and maintain occupational health and disease prevention programs. Employers in specified Standard 

[22:2:58,703] Industrial Classification codes who employ 10 or more qualifying employees are subject to the fee. The BOE administers the 

[22:3:58,712] program in partnership with the California Department of Public Health.

[2:0:58,73] 0570300 - INTEGRATED WASTE MANAGEMENT PROGRAM 

[3:0:58,91] This program provides revenue for the Integrated Waste Management Account in the Integrated Waste Management Fund. 

[3:1:58,100] The fees provide funding to respond to potential health and environmental problems at on-site and off-site solid waste 

[3:2:58,109] landfills, and supports state and local landfill permit enforcement programs. Operators of solid waste disposal facilities that 

[3:3:58,118] include non-hazardous wood waste facilities are subject to the fee. The BOE administers the program in partnership with 

[3:4:58,127] CalRecycle. 

[4:0:58,145] 0570325 - UNDERGROUND STORAGE TANK FEE PROGRAM 

[5:0:58,163] This program provides revenue for the Underground Storage Tank (UST) Cleanup Fund in the State Treasury. BOE collects 

[5:1:58,172] a fee for each gallon of petroleum placed in USTs for the Petroleum Underground Storage Tank Financing Account. This 

[5:2:58,181] revenue provides funding to monitor and regulate underground storage tanks containing petroleum, reimburse businesses 

[5:3:58,190] for the cleanup of leaking USTs, and protect human health and the environment. 

[6:0:58,208] 0570350 - OIL SPILL PREVENTION PROGRAM 

[7:0:58,226] This program provides revenue to the Department of Fish and Wildlife, which is deposited into the Oil Spill Prevention and 

[7:1:58,235] Administration Fund. Fees are collected on all crude oil and petroleum products received in California via marine pipelines 

[7:2:58,244] and terminals. The prevention and administration fees provide funding to implement oil spill prevention programs and 

[7:3:58,253] reimburse the member agencies of the State Interagency Oil Spill Committee for costs arising from the implementation of 

[7:4:58,262] this program. Funding is also provided to implement, install, and maintain emergency programs, equipment, and facilities to 

[7:5:58,271] respond to, contain, and cleanup oil spills. 

[8:0:58,289] 0570375 - ENERGY RESOURCES SURCHARGE PROGRAM 

[9:0:58,307] This program provides revenue for the Energy Resource Surcharge Fund and is used to support the State Energy 

[9:1:58,316] Resources Conservation and Development Commission. The revenue is generated by administering a surcharge on 

[9:2:58,325] consumers of electrical energy purchased from an electrical utility. 

[10:0:58,343] 0570400 - ANNUAL WATER RIGHTS FEE PROGRAM 

[11:0:58,361] This program provides revenue for the Water Rights Fund. The fees provide funding to the State Water Resources Control 

[11:1:58,370] Board to support the activities of its Division of Water Rights. The annual fee is collected from water right permit holders 

[11:2:58,379] based on a schedule of fees adopted each fiscal year by the State Water Resources Control Board.  

[12:0:58,397] 0570425 - CHILDHOOD LEAD POISONING PREVENTION FEE PROGRAM 

[13:0:58,415] This program provides revenue for the Childhood Lead Poisoning Prevention Fund. This program collects an annual fee 

[13:1:58,424] from architectural coatings distributors, motor vehicle fuel distributors, and facilities currently reporting releases of lead into 

[13:2:58,433] ambient air in California. This revenue supports the Childhood Lead Poisoning Prevention Fee Program administered by the 

[13:3:58,442] California Department of Public Health, Childhood Lead Poisoning Prevention Branch. 

[14:0:58,460] 0570450 - MARINE INVASIVE SPECIES PROGRAM 

[15:0:58,478] This program provides revenue for the Marine Invasive Species Control Fund and is often referred to as the Ballast Water 

[15:1:58,487] Management Program. The fees provide funding to the California State Lands Commission to prevent or minimize the 

[15:2:58,496] introduction and spread of non-indigenous aquatic species into California waters. Owners or operators of qualifying vessels 

[15:3:58,505] carrying, or capable of carrying, ballast water from outside California are subject to the fee. The BOE administers the 

[15:4:58,514] program in partnership with the Commission. 

[16:0:58,532] 0570475 - FIRE PREVENTION FEE PROGRAM 

[17:0:58,550] This program provides revenue for the State Responsibility Area Fire Prevention Fund. The revenue is generated by 

[17:1:58,559] administering an annual fire prevention fee charged on each habitable structure on a parcel that is within a state 

[17:2:58,568] responsibility area. The revenues are to be used by the California Department of Forestry and Fire Protection for fire 

[17:3:58,577] prevention activities within the State Responsibility Area which benefits those owners who are subject to the fire prevention 

[17:4:58,586] fee. 

[18:0:58,604] 0570500 - EMERGENCY TELEPHONE USERS SURCHARGE PROGRAM 

[19:0:58,622] This program provides revenue for the State Emergency Telephone Number Account. Revenue generated by this program 

[19:1:58,631] funds the State's "911" emergency telephone system by administering a surcharge on intrastate telephone and Voice over 

[19:2:58,640] Internet Protocol (VoIP) communication services.  

[20:0:58,658] 0570525 - E-WASTE RECYCLING FEE PROGRAM

[21:1:58,685] Management Fund. The fees provide funding for CalRecycle by imposing a recycling fee upon the retail sale or lease of new 

[21:2:58,694] or refurbished video display devices identified by the Department of Toxic Substances as containing hazardous materials.

[7:0:58,208] 0570625 - APPEALS FROM OTHER GOVERNMENTAL PROGRAMS 

[8:0:58,226] This program reviews income tax assessments and corporation taxes and eligibility determinations made in administering 

[8:1:58,235] the Senior Citizens Property Tax Assistance Program upon written request filed by a taxpayer. The program also acts as an 

[8:2:58,244] impartial tribunal to hear and decide property tax assessment appeals by a local government (or one of its agencies) that

[10:0:58,298] This program provides revenue to the Prepaid Mobile Telephony Services (MTS) Surcharge Fund and the Local Charges for 

[10:1:58,307] the Prepaid MTS Fund. The revenue funds the State Emergency Telephone Number Account, universal service funds and 

[10:2:58,316] local funds. A surcharge is imposed on each consumer of prepaid mobile telephony services at the retail level. 

[11:0:58,334] 0570675 - REGIONAL RAILROAD ACCIDENT PREPAREDNESS AND IMMEDIATE RESPONSE PROGRAM 

[12:0:58,352] This program provides revenue to the Governor's Office of Emergency Services, to prepare for and provide immediate onsite 

[12:1:58,361] response related to a large-scale release of hazardous materials from a rail car or a railroad accident involving a rail car. 

[12:2:58,370] The revenues are deposited into the Regional Railroad Accident Preparedness and Immediate Response Fund. Fees are 

[12:3:58,379] collected on the top 25 most hazardous material commodities transported by rail car within California. The fee provides 

[12:4:58,388] funding to pay for the planning, developing, support, and maintenance of various aspects of regional, state, and local 

[12:5:58,397] emergency response programs, teams, specialized equipment, supplies, and training to prepare for such an occurrence. 

[13:0:58,415] 0570700 - LEAD-ACID BATTERY RECYCLING FEE PROGRAM 

[14:0:58,433] This program provides revenue to the Lead-Acid Battery Cleanup Fund. The fee provides funding for investigation, site 

[14:1:58,442] evaluation, cleanup, remediation, removal, monitoring, and other response actions for areas contaminated due to lead-acid 

[14:2:58,451] battery recycling facility operations, as well as refund payments, loan repayments, and administrative costs. Lead-acid 

[14:3:58,460] battery manufacturers and consumers are subject to the fees. The BOE administers the program in partnership with the 

[14:4:58,469] California Department of Toxic Substances Control. This program creates the California Battery Fee and the Manufacturer 

[14:5:58,478] Battery Fee. 

[15:0:58,496] 0570725 - CANNABIS TAXES PROGRAM 

[16:0:58,514] This program imposes an excise tax on the retail purchase of medical and recreational cannabis and a cultivation tax on the 

[16:1:58,523] dry weight of flowers and leaves of cannabis harvested for sale. The excise tax is imposed upon the purchaser of the 

[16:2:58,532] cannabis and the retailer is required to collect and remit the tax. The cultivation tax is imposed upon the person harvesting 

[16:3:58,541] cannabis that enters the commercial marketplace. These taxes provide funding for youth education and prevention 

[16:4:58,550] programs, environmental mitigation efforts, law enforcement, and administration costs for numerous state agencies charged 

[16:5:58,559] with licensing, regulating, and taxing the cultivation and sale of cannabis.

[14:0:234,425] 0890 Secretary of State 

[14:1:57,445] The Secretary of State, a constitutionally established office, is the chief elections officer of the state and is responsible for 

[14:2:57,454] the administration and enforcement of election laws. The Office also is responsible for administering and enforcing laws 

[14:3:57,463] pertaining to filing documents associated with corporations, limited liability companies, partnerships, limited partnerships, 

[14:4:57,472] unincorporated associations and pertaining to filing bonds and perfecting security agreements. In addition, the Office is 

[14:5:57,481] responsible for commissioning notaries public, enforcing the notary laws, and in conjunction with being the home of the State 

[14:6:57,490] Archives, administering a state records management program and preserving documents and records having historical 

[14:7:57,499] significance. The Secretary of State is the filing officer for lobbying and campaign registration and disclosure documents filed 

[14:8:57,508] under the Political Reform Act. The Secretary of State also operates the Safe at Home program, maintains the Domestic 

[14:9:57,517] Partners and Advance Health Care Directives registries, provides support functions for the Voting Modernization Board, and 

[14:10:57,526] is home to the California Museum. 

[15:0:58,544] Policy associated with the administration of the Office is accomplished through the divisions of Elections, Political Reform, 

[15:1:58,553] Business Programs, Archives, Information Technology, and Management Services.

[11:0:58,463] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[12:0:58,491] 0700 - FILINGS AND REGISTRATIONS 

[13:0:58,509] The Business Programs Division is comprised of three primary areas: Business Entities, Uniform Commercial Code, and 

[13:1:58,518] Notary Public and Special Filings. 

[14:0:58,536] Business Entities examines, files, and maintains formation documents for new California business entities and qualifies out-

[14:1:58,545] of-state and international entities to conduct business in California; and also examines, files and maintains changes to the 

[14:2:58,554] records of domestic or qualified foreign business entities to ensure the business entities are properly formed, merged, 

[14:3:58,563] converted, amended, and dissolved in compliance with California law. Statements of Information containing key officers and 

[14:4:58,572] contact information are also processed and maintained for public and governmental use. 

[15:0:58,590] Uniform Commercial Code files certain financing statements allowing lending institutions to protect their financial interest in 

[15:1:58,599] personal property and established priority in case of debtor default or bankruptcy. Notices of judgment liens, attachment 

[15:2:58,608] liens, agricultural liens, and equipment liens are also filed in Uniform Commercial Code, as well as notices of various tax 

[15:3:58,617] liens submitted by state and federal taxing agencies such as the Franchise Tax Board and the Internal Revenue Service. 

[15:4:58,635] Notary Public and Special Filings appoints and commissions qualified notaries public for four- year terms, reviews and 

[15:5:58,644] approves notary public education courses, and certifies to the authenticity of signatures of notaries public and public officials 

[15:6:58,653] on documents for use in foreign countries. Special Filings include trademarks and service marks as well as surety bonds that 

[15:7:58,662] certain business entities are required to file, notices of joint power agreements, city and county charters, and claims for 

[15:8:58,671] successor-in-interest. This area also has disciplinary functions with regard to notaries public and immigration consultants. 

[15:9:58,689] The Advance Health Care Directive (AHCD) Registry maintains AHCDs, which allow a person to indicate his/her medical 

[15:10:58,698] treatment preferences if he/she cannot speak or make decisions for him/herself. The AHCD also may designate someone 

[15:11:58,707] else to make decisions regarding medical treatment. AHCDs and related information can be provided upon request to the 

[15:12:58,716] registrant's health care provider, public guardian, or legal representative. 

[16:0:58,745] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details. 


# === PAGE 205 === [size: 612x792]
[0:0:58,15] LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE   2017-18 STATE BUDGET — LJE 203 

[1:0:199,44] 0890 Secretary of State - Continued 

[2:0:58,73] The Domestic Partners Registry registers same-sex couples regardless of the age of the partners, and opposite-sex couples 

[2:1:58,82] in which one partner is at least 62 years old, as domestic partners in California. 

[3:0:58,100] The Victims of Corporate Fraud Compensation Fund provides limited restitution to victims of corporate fraud who are unable 

[3:1:58,109] to collect through other means on a judgment against a corporation for corporate fraud. 

[4:0:58,127] Safe at Home is a confidential mail forwarding program designed to assist victims of domestic violence, sexual assault, 

[4:1:58,136] stalking, or a reproductive healthcare employee, patient, or volunteer. Participants in the Safe at Home program are 

[4:2:58,145] provided with a free post office box to use as a substitute mailing address, thereby protecting their actual residential 

[4:3:58,154] address. Once enrolled into the program, Safe at Home serves as a liaison for those participants who qualify for additional 

[4:4:58,163] confidential services offered by various state and local agencies. 

[5:0:58,181] 0705 - ELECTIONS 

[6:0:58,199] The Secretary of State, as California's chief elections officer, has broad responsibility to administer the election process. This 

[6:1:58,208] program oversees all federal and state elections within California, maintaining a statewide database of all registered voters, 

[6:2:58,217] tracks and certifies ballot measures, certifies candidates, and certifies election results. In addition, the program oversees the 

[6:3:58,226] modernization of voting equipment and the improvement of current electoral database systems, enhancing the voting 

[6:4:58,235] processes, providing accessibility to voters, working to increase people's knowledge of the electoral system, and 

[6:5:58,244] investigates election related criminal violations as provided by California Elections Code. 

[7:0:58,262] This program includes the campaign and lobbying registration and disclosure provisions of the Political Reform Act of 1974. 

[7:1:58,271] Under this law, the Office registers all levels of campaign committees, and reviews for compliance with statutory 

[7:2:58,280] requirements all state-level candidate and campaign recipient committees, major donors, slate mailer, political party, and 

[7:3:58,289] independent expenditure committees. The program registers lobbyists (including placement agents), lobbying firms and 

[7:4:58,298] lobbyist employers, reviews for compliance with statutory requirements the periodic financial disclosure reports filed by 

[7:5:58,307] lobbying entities, and publishes a Lobbying Directory on the Internet. This program also supports the electronic filing 

[7:6:58,316] requirements of the Political Reform Act and posts relevant registration and disclosure information to the Office's web site so 

[7:7:58,325] the public can track where campaign money is raised and spent and what lobbying activity is occurring in state government. 

[7:8:58,334] A searchable database of campaign and lobbying financial activity is also provided through the web site. 

[8:0:58,352] 0710 - ARCHIVES 

[9:0:58,370] The California State Archives establishes and administers a records management program that applies efficient and 

[9:1:58,379] economical management methods to the creation, utilization, maintenance, retention, preservation, and disposal of state 

[9:2:58,388] records and acquires, indexes, preserves, and provides reference access to irreplaceable historic materials from the three 

[9:3:58,397] branches of state government. The Archives acquires physical and electronic records with legal, administrative or 

[9:4:58,406] evidentiary value, or that have historical significance. Materials are transferred to the Archives for permanent preservation. 

[10:0:58,424] 9900 - ADMINISTRATION 

[11:0:58,442] This program develops and manages overall policy. It serves as the liaison to other state agencies, the Legislature, the 

[11:1:58,451] federal government, and other states' Secretaries of State. This program responds to constituent correspondence and 

[11:2:58,460] requests from the public and advocates in the Legislature, administers the Secretary's role as a member of the National 

[11:3:58,469] Association of Secretaries of State, in the management of task forces and advisory committees, in the implementation of 

[11:4:58,478] new federal and state statutory requirements, and coordinates and disseminates information about the Office and its 

[11:5:58,487] initiatives to the public. It also provides the Office with the necessary personnel, general administrative, budgeting, fiscal 

[11:6:58,496] services, and information technology expertise to plan, develop, implement, and operate innovative and effective business 

[11:7:58,505] and information systems solutions.

[1:0:241,44] 0950 State Treasurer 

[1:1:58,64] The State Treasurer, a constitutionally established office, provides banking services for state government with goals to 

[1:2:58,73] minimize interest and service costs and to maximize yield on investments. The Treasurer is responsible for the custody of all 

[1:3:58,82] monies and securities belonging to or held in trust by the state; investment of temporarily idle state monies; administration of 

[1:4:58,91] the sale of state bonds, their redemption and interest payments; and payment of warrants or checks drawn by the State 

[1:5:58,100] Controller and other state agencies.

[8:0:58,177] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[9:0:58,204] 0740010 - INVESTMENT SERVICES 

[10:0:58,222] The Investment Division is responsible for investment of state monies from the date of receipt through the date of 

[10:1:58,231] redemption. During the 2015-16 fiscal year, this Division handled 7,359 security investment transactions totaling $312.9 

[10:2:58,240] billion. The Pooled Money Investment Board (PMIB) program accounted for 5,337 of these transactions totaling $266.1 

[10:3:58,249] billion; time deposits accounted for 1,599 transactions totaling $37.5 billion. The remaining $9.3 billion is invested on behalf 

[10:4:58,258] of the state's special funds, such as those associated with the California Housing Finance Agency, the Department of Fish 

[10:5:58,267] and Wildlife, the state's retirement system, etc. The Division also administers the Local Agency Investment Fund (LAIF), a 

[10:6:58,276] voluntary investment program created to offer California local agencies greater access to the financial markets through the 

[10:7:58,285] PMIB program. In the 2015-16 fiscal year, 2,479 local agencies participated in LAIF, with deposits averaging $20.9 billion for 

[10:8:58,294] the fiscal year. 

[11:0:58,312] 0740019 - CENTRALIZED TREASURY AND SECURITIES MANAGEMENT 

[12:0:58,330] In 1949, the California Legislature amended Government Code Section 16305 to create the Centralized Treasury System 

[12:1:58,339] (CTS) thereby requiring agencies of the State to deposit their money in trust with the Treasurer. The legislation also requires 

[12:2:58,348] the Treasurer to safeguard the money and make safe and prudent investments. In 1955, the Legislature created the PMIB, 

[12:3:58,357] giving the Board the responsibility to designate the amount of money available for the investment in securities, bank 

[12:4:58,366] deposits, and loans to the General Fund. 

[13:0:58,384] The Centralized Treasury and Securities Management Division (CTSMD) oversees all banking aspects of the CTS. The goal 

[13:1:58,393] of the CTSMD is to maximize the earning of interest consistent with safe and prudent treasury management, and to ensure 

[13:2:58,402] that the depository banks provide the state with proper and adequate security for the deposit of state monies. The State 

[13:3:58,411] Treasurer maintains demand bank accounts with eight banks for the purpose of providing necessary statewide depository 

[13:4:58,420] coverage for the remittance of funds collected by the various state agencies. 

[14:0:58,438] The CTSMD 1) monitors the cash flow of all state funds, forecasts cash balances, revenue, expenditures, and the amounts 

[14:1:58,447] available for daily investments, 2) ensures accurate and timely agency deposits, 3) administers and executes the wire 

[14:2:58,456] transfer of funds, 4) reconciles state accounts with depository banks and redeems all state items submitted by presenting 

[14:3:58,465] banks for payments, 5) executes the clearance and income collection for state investments (excluding PERS and STRS) 

[14:4:58,474] and securities pledged to the state, 6) fulfills the clearance and settlement of securities pledged to the state for the time, 

[14:5:58,483] demand, and other state agency programs, and 7) is responsible for the safekeeping of securities and other personal 

[14:6:58,492] property owned by or pledged to the state. 

[15:0:58,510] 0740028 - PUBLIC FINANCE 

[16:0:58,528] The Public Finance Division is responsible for selling State of California general obligation bonds, commercial paper notes, 

[16:1:58,537] revenue anticipation notes, lease revenue bonds, revenue bonds, and any other indebtedness for all state agencies. The 

[16:2:58,546] Division provides debt administration services for most state bonds and is responsible for disseminating information to 

[16:3:58,555] bondholders through the Investor Relations Program. 

[17:0:58,573] The Division also assures compliance with federal tax laws applicable to state debt so there is no adverse consequences to 

[17:1:58,582] bondholders or increased borrowing costs to the state. The post-issuance tax compliance for various state debt includes 

[17:2:58,591] monitoring the use of bond proceeds, monitoring use of bond financed property, tracking expenditures, managing rebate and 

[17:3:58,600] yield restriction compliance, coordinating necessary financial disclosure, and ensuring proper record keeping. 

[18:0:58,618] 0740035 - ADMINISTRATION AND INFORMATION SERVICES 

[19:0:58,636] The Administration Division, Executive Office, and the Information Services Division provide executive direction and support 

[19:1:58,645] services to programs in the State Treasurer's Office. Services include budgeting, personnel, accounting, information 

[19:2:58,654] systems, business services, technical support, and production operations. 

[20:0:58,672] 9900 - ADMINISTRATION AND INFORMATION SERVICES 

[21:0:58,690] The Administration Division, Executive Office, and the Information Services Division provide executive direction and support 

[21:1:58,699] services to programs in the State Treasurer's Office. Services include budgeting, personnel, accounting, information 

[21:2:58,708] systems, business services, technical support, and production operations. Starting with the 2017-18 Governor's Budget, the 

[21:3:58,717] Administration program is shown separately. 

[22:0:58,745] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[15:5:58,707] dependents of California residents killed in the terrorist attacks of September 11, 2001.

[4:0:58,153] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[5:0:58,180] 0780 - GOLDEN STATE SCHOLARSHARE COLLEGE SAVINGS TRUST PROGRAM 

[5:1:58,198] The Golden State ScholarShare College Savings Trust Program is California's state-sponsored 529 college savings plan 

[5:2:58,207] established to help families save for higher education. Earnings are tax-free when used for qualified higher education 

[5:3:58,216] expenses (such as tuition, fees, supplies, books, and certain room and board expenses) at eligible educational institutions. 

[5:4:58,234] 0785 - GOVERNOR'S SCHOLARSHIP PROGRAMS 

[6:0:58,252] The Governor's Scholarship Programs (GSP) rewarded public school students who demonstrated high academic 

[6:1:58,261] achievement with scholarships. Students may have earned multiple $1,000 Governor's Scholars Awards and a one-time 

[6:2:58,270] $2,500 Governor's Distinguished Mathematics and Science Scholars Award for scores attained on tests taken in 2000, 2001, 

[6:3:58,279] and 2002. GSP became inoperative and was repealed after 2002. ScholarShare administers scholarship awards that were 

[6:4:58,288] already earned. 

[7:0:58,306] 0790 - CALIFORNIA MEMORIAL SCHOLARSHIP PROGRAM 

[8:0:58,324] The California Memorial Scholarship Program provides scholarships to surviving dependents of California residents killed as 

[8:1:58,333] a result of the terrorist attacks of September 11, 2001.

[5:0:163,213] 0959 California Debt Limit Allocation Committee 

[6:0:58,233] The California Debt Limit Allocation Committee's mission is to allocate tax-exempt private activity bond authority for the State 

[6:1:58,242] of California. Private activity bonds may only be used by the private sector for projects and programs that provide a public 

[6:2:58,251] benefit, such as the creation of affordable housing. 

[7:0:58,269] The federal government limits the amount of tax-exempt private activity bond authority that can be issued on an annual 

[7:1:58,278] basis. Except for the Qualified Public Educational Facility Bond Program, the bond authority limit is calculated by multiplying 

[7:2:58,287] the state population by $100. The state debt (or tax-exempt bond) limit totaled over $3.92 billion in 2017. The limit for the 

[7:3:58,296] Qualified Public Educational Facility Bond Program is calculated by multiplying the state population by $10, and totaled $392 

[7:4:58,305] million for 2017. 

[8:0:58,323] The Committee's allocation of tax-exempt bond authority results in the issuance of bonds by cities, counties, joint powers 

[8:1:58,332] authorities and state agencies. The bonds are purchased and used by the private sector and are not an obligation of the 

[8:2:58,341] state or of the federal government. 

[9:0:58,359] The Committee administers 10 programs that are funded through the allocation and issuance of tax-exempt private activity 

[9:1:58,368] bonds, and is also responsible for the reallocation of Qualified Energy Conservation Bond (QECB) authority originally 

[9:2:58,377] provided to qualified localities, but later waived back to the state. The QECB program, made available through the American 

[9:3:58,386] Recovery and Reinvestment Act of 2009, provides tax incentives and lower borrowing costs for local governments and 

[9:4:58,395] private entities to promote job creation and economic recovery in areas particularly affected by employment decline and to 

[9:5:58,404] facilitate renewable energy conservation programs and projects throughout the state. 

[9:6:58,422] The Committee is funded on a fee-supported basis and is comprised of the State Treasurer as Chairperson, the Governor, 

[9:7:58,431] or upon his designation, the Director of Finance, and the State Controller.

[15:0:58,304] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[16:0:58,331] 0810 - CALIFORNIA DEBT LIMIT ALLOCATION COMMITTEE 

[17:0:58,349] Specified entities can issue various bonds, including mortgage revenue bonds (MRBs) that support below-market interest 

[17:1:58,358] rates for the specified loans; and mortgage credit certificates (MCCs) that are used to reduce a homebuyer's federal tax 

[17:2:58,367] liability. Below is a discussion of each program: 

[18:0:58,385] Qualified Residential Rental Project Program: 

[19:0:58,394] These tax-exempt housing revenue bonds assist developers of multifamily rental housing units to acquire land and construct 

[19:1:58,403] new units or purchase and rehabilitate existing units. The tax-exempt bonds lower the interest rate on a mortgage to be paid 

[19:2:58,412] by the developers. The developers, in turn, produce affordable and market rate rental housing for low and very low-income 

[19:3:58,421] households by reducing rental rates to these individuals and families. Projects that receive an award of bond authority have 

[19:4:58,430] the right to apply for non-competitive four-percent tax credits. 

[20:0:58,448] Single-Family Housing Program: 

[21:0:58,457] These tax-exempt MRBs or MCCs assist first-time homebuyers with purchasing homes. Homebuyers may purchase single-

[21:1:58,466] family homes, either freestanding or detached, condominiums, or townhouses. Program participants must meet income 

[21:2:58,475] limits and must purchase a home that falls within the program's purchase price limitations. 

[22:0:58,493] Home Improvement and Rehabilitation Bond Program: 

[23:0:58,502] MRBs or MCCs may be used to assist homeowners with home improvement financing. Homeowners may improve single-

[23:1:58,511] family homes, either freestanding or detached, condominiums, or townhouses. Program participants must meet income 

[23:2:58,520] limits, and in certain cases, must own a home that falls within the program's rehabilitation cost and age-of-home limitations. 

[24:0:58,538] Extra Credit Home Purchase Program: 

[25:0:58,547] These MRBs or MCCs assist teachers, principals and other eligible school staff with purchasing homes. 

[26:0:58,565] Industrial Development Bond Project Program: 

[27:0:58,574] Small-Issue industrial development bonds are tax-exempt private activity bonds that are issued to assist manufacturing 

[27:1:58,583] facilities finance capital expenditures. These bonds offer interest rate savings to small and midsize manufacturers in 

[27:2:58,592] contrast to conventional loans, and help manufacturers retain and create new jobs within their communities. 

[28:0:58,610] Exempt Facility Program: 

[29:0:58,619] Exempt Facility Bonds are tax-exempt private activity bonds that are issued to finance solid waste disposal and waste 

[29:1:58,628] recycling facilities. The tax-exempt bonds provide facility owners with low-cost financing in the form of below-market interest 

[29:2:58,637] rate loans. The interest rate savings enable the project owners to maintain lower customer rates or minimize customer rate 

[29:3:58,646] increases, while at the same time assisting the communities they serve to meet mandated requirements to protect and 

[29:4:58,655] enhance the environment. 

[30:0:58,673] Student Loan Program: 

[31:0:58,682] Student Loan Bonds are tax-exempt private activity bonds issued for the purpose of either financing direct loans to college 

[31:1:58,691] students and their parents or purchasing bundles of already-originated loans on the secondary market. When used for direct 

[31:2:58,700] lending programs, tax-exempt bond allocation allows lenders to pass on interest rate savings to financially needy students 

[31:3:58,709] via below-market interest rate loans. 

[32:0:58,727] Beginning Farmer Program: 

[33:0:58,745] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details. 


# === PAGE 228 === [size: 612x792]
[0:0:58,15] 2017-18 STATE BUDGET — LJE 226   LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE 

[1:0:128,44] 0959 California Debt Limit Allocation Committee - Continued 

[2:0:58,73] Beginning Farmer Bonds are tax-exempt private activity bonds that are issued to back below-market interest rate financing 

[2:1:58,82] for eligible agricultural land, construction/improvements, breeder livestock and equipment for qualified farmers. Eligibility, 

[2:2:58,91] permissible items, and loan limits are set by the United States Internal Revenue Code. Under the program, a conduit bond 

[2:3:58,100] issuer applies to the Committee for an allocation of Beginning Farmer Bonds. If the Committee approves the allocation, the 

[2:4:58,109] issuer then brings together farmers, financial institutions, contract sellers or investors to negotiate terms of a transaction. 

[2:5:58,127] Qualified Public Educational Facility Bond Program: 

[3:0:58,136] Qualified Public Educational Facility Bonds (QPEF's) are tax-exempt private activity bonds issued to finance the 

[3:1:58,145] construction, renovation, and furnishing of primary and secondary school facilities. This form of financing reduces the cost of 

[3:2:58,154] financing for schools as interest earned by the lender is tax exempt. 

[3:3:58,172] Qualified Energy Conservation Bond Program: 

[4:0:58,181] Qualified Energy Conservation Bonds (QECBs) may be issued as either tax-exempt private activity bonds or governmental 

[4:1:58,190] purpose taxable bonds. When issued as a governmental purpose taxable bond, QECBs provide the issuer with either a 

[4:2:58,199] direct or tax credit interest subsidy. QECBs may be issued to finance a broad array of qualified conservation purposes such 

[4:3:58,208] as capital expenditures, research facilities and research grant programs, mass commuting facilities, public education 

[4:4:58,217] campaigns and demonstration projects.

[10:0:58,335] The Authority was established to assist transportation agencies in obtaining financing to develop transportation projects. To 

[10:1:58,344] meet this objective, statutes allow the Authority to issue, or to approve specified project sponsors to issue, revenue bonds to 

[10:2:58,353] fund transportation projects backed in whole or in part, by various revenue streams of transportation funds (including toll 

[10:3:58,362] revenues). Statutes provide the authority to approve the imposition and collection of tolls on proposed transportation projects 

[10:4:58,371] under certain conditions. The planning, programming, and allocation of transportation projects are performed by the 

[10:5:58,380] California Transportation Commission and the California Department of Transportation, as appropriate. 

[11:0:95,422] 0965 California Industrial Development Financing Advisory Commission 

[11:1:58,443] The California Industrial Development Financing Advisory Commission creates employment opportunities and supports local 

[11:2:58,452] economic development by approving local entities' issuance of industrial development bonds. These bonds provide 

[11:3:58,461] manufacturers with a low-cost financing option to build, expand, or equip their facilities in California. The Commission 

[11:4:58,470] independently reviews bond applications to ensure compliance with federal tax law and state law, provides technical 

[11:5:58,479] assistance to bond issuers, and approves the bond sales by local authorities. 

[12:0:58,497] The State Treasurer serves as chairperson of the Commission. The other members are the Director of the Department of 

[12:1:58,506] Finance, the State Controller, the Director of the Governor's Office of Business and Economic Development, and the 

[12:2:58,515] Commissioner of the Department of Business Oversight.

[11:0:58,311] 0830 - CALIFORNIA INDUSTRIAL DEVELOPMENT FINANCING ADVISORY COMMISSION 

[12:0:58,329] The core program area is the Industrial Development Bond Program, under which the Commission serves as the mandatory 

[12:1:58,338] approval agency for the local bond issuers. Once potential borrowers (manufacturers and processing companies) apply 

[12:2:58,347] through their local government agency for low cost tax-exempt financing, the Commission carefully reviews the public 

[12:3:58,356] benefits generated by the proposed project, particularly those benefits associated with job creation, and determines whether 

[12:4:58,365] these benefits will significantly outweigh any detrimental public effects. Eligible capital expenditures include the acquisition 

[12:5:58,374] of land, building construction, building renovation, and the purchase of machinery and equipment. Bond proceeds also can 

[12:6:58,383] be used to cover the cost of architects, engineers, attorneys, permits, and the cost of bond issuance. The local issuer can 

[12:7:58,392] be a city, county, economic development authority, or a joint power authority.

[1:0:163,44] 0968 California Tax Credit Allocation Committee 

[2:0:57,64] The mission of the California Tax Credit Allocation Committee is to fairly allocate federal and state tax credits to create and 

[2:1:57,73] maintain safe quality affordable rental housing for low-income households in California by forming partnerships with 

[2:2:57,82] developers, investors and public entities. 

[3:0:57,100] The Committee works in public/private partnerships to assist with low-income multi-family rental housing project 

[3:1:57,109] development, while fulfilling its responsibilities as a credit agency through project compliance monitoring. The Committee 

[3:2:57,118] also coordinates its functions with state and local housing fund providers and with private fund investors, when providing and 

[3:3:57,127] maintaining quality, affordable housing. 

[4:0:57,145] The Committee consists of seven members, including the Treasurer who is designated as Chairperson, the Governor or 

[4:1:57,154] Director of Finance, the State Controller, the Director of the Department of Housing and Community Development, the 

[4:2:57,163] Executive Director of the California Housing Finance Agency, and two local government representatives.

[0:0:58,15] 2017-18 STATE BUDGET — LJE 232   LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE 

[1:0:128,44] 0968 California Tax Credit Allocation Committee - Continued 

[2:0:58,95] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[3:0:58,123] 0840 - CALIFORNIA TAX CREDIT ALLOCATION COMMITTEE 

[3:1:58,141] The Federal Low-Income Housing Tax-Credit Program: 

[4:0:58,159] Congress authorized the federal program in 1986. It replaced traditional housing tax incentives, such as accelerated 

[4:1:58,168] depreciation, with a tax credit that enables developers of affordable rental housing to raise project equity through the "sale" 

[4:2:58,177] of tax benefits to investors. 

[5:0:58,195] The annual housing credit ceiling is indexed for inflation. As of 2016, each state has an annual housing credit ceiling of 

[5:1:58,204] $2.35 per state resident, and may qualify for a share of credits available annually in a national pool comprised of states' 

[5:2:58,213] unused credits. Investors can take the annual credit against their federal income tax liability each year for a ten-year period. 

[5:3:58,231] The State Low-Income Housing Tax-Credit Program: 

[6:0:58,249] Recognizing the high cost of developing housing in California, the California Legislature authorized the State Low-Income 

[6:1:58,258] Housing Tax-Credit Program to augment the federal tax credit program. Specifically, projects that are not receiving an 

[6:2:58,267] increase in their federal tax credit basis may apply for and receive state tax credits. However, an exception to this rule is in 

[6:3:58,276] place for projects serving special needs populations (as defined in Section 10325 of the California Code of Regulations). 

[6:4:58,285] Those projects may apply for and receive state tax credits even if they are receiving an increase in their federal tax credit 

[6:5:58,294] basis. The project's "eligible basis" is the portion of the total project cost that is used to calculate the amount of the tax credit. 

[6:6:58,312] The annual state credit ceiling is currently $94.5 million, indexed for inflation. Investors take the state credit over a four-year 

[6:7:58,321] period in contrast to the ten-year federal allocation period. 

[6:8:58,339] Tax-Exempt Bond Financed Program: 

[7:0:58,357] Developments financed with tax-exempt bond proceeds may also receive federal tax credit. The sponsors of such projects 

[7:1:58,366] must apply to the Committee and must conform to applicable federal and state statutory and regulatory requirements, but 

[7:2:58,375] there is no annual cap on the amount of credit that may be awarded by the state to such developments. The annual credit 

[7:3:58,384] available is based on approximately four percent of the qualified basis of the development. The qualified basis includes 

[7:4:58,393] those costs attributable to the units that will be income and rent restricted for a minimum of 30 years. 

[7:5:58,411] Under federal law, credit projects must remain affordable for at least 30 years; however, California's program generally 

[7:6:58,420] requires maintaining affordability for 55 years. Land use agreements are recorded against each credit project to ensure 

[7:7:58,429] compliance. 

[8:0:58,447] Farmworker Housing Tax-Credit Program: 

[9:0:58,465] Chapter 521, Statutes of 2008 folded the previous Farmworker Housing Assistance tax credits into the general state low-

[9:1:58,474] income housing tax-credit program. While $500,000 annually continues to be authorized for state tax credits in support of 

[9:2:58,483] farmworker housing, the program now operates under the rules of the general state low-income housing tax-credit program. 

[10:0:58,509] DETAILED EXPENDITURES BY PROGRAM

[11:0:58,574] 0971 California Alternative Energy and Advanced Transportation Financing Authority 

[11:1:58,594] The California Alternative Energy and Advanced Transportation Financing Authority was established by Chapter 908, 

[11:2:58,603] Statutes of 1980, to promote the prompt and efficient development of energy sources which are renewable or which more 

[11:3:58,612] efficiently utilize and conserve scarce energy resources. Recognizing the importance of developing a secure energy future 

[11:4:58,621] to protect the environment and ensure economic stability, the Authority advances the state's goals of reducing greenhouse 

[11:5:58,630] gas emissions by providing financing options to assist industries in increasing the deployment of sustainable and renewable 

[11:6:58,639] energy sources, implementing measures that increase the efficiency of the use of energy, creating high quality employment 

[11:7:58,648] opportunities, and lessening the state's dependence on fossil fuels. To support these goals, the Authority provides financing 

[11:8:58,657] and credit enhancements to promote the establishment of facilities that use alternative methods and sources of energy, and 

[11:9:58,666] facilities needed for the development and commercialization of advanced transportation technologies. 

[11:10:58,684] The Authority consists of five members: the State Treasurer, who serves as the chairperson, the State Controller, the 

[11:11:58,693] Director of the Department of Finance, the Chairperson of the State Energy Resources Conservation and Development 

[11:12:58,702] Commission, and the President of the Public Utilities Commission. 

[12:0:58,745] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[1:0:58,44] 0971 California Alternative Energy and Advanced Transportation Financing Authority 

[1:1:272,62] - Continued 

[2:0:58,100] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[3:0:58,127] 0850 - ALTERNATIVE ENERGY AND ADVANCED TRANSPORTATION FINANCING AUTHORITY 

[4:0:58,145] Financial assistance can take the form of loans, loan loss reserves, interest rate reductions, proceeds of bonds issued by the 

[4:1:58,154] authority, bond insurance, loan guarantees or other credit enhancements or liquidity facilities, contributions of money, or a 

[4:2:58,163] combination thereof, as determined and approved by resolution of the Authority. 

[5:0:58,181] In 2010, the Authority launched a sales and use tax exclusion (STE) program for advanced transportation and alternative 

[5:1:58,190] source manufacturing in California (Chapter 10, Statutes of 2010) and subsequently, Chapter 677, Statutes of 2012, 

[5:2:58,199] expanded the STE program to include advanced manufacturing, with an annual cap of $100 million available for STE 

[5:3:58,208] awards. Chapter 768, Statutes of 2015, further expanded the program to also include equipment primarily used to process 

[5:4:58,217] recycled feedstock and equipment that primarily utilizes recycled feedstock in the production of another product. The 

[5:5:58,226] objective of this program is to promote the creation of California-based manufacturing, businesses, and jobs that are aimed 

[5:6:58,235] at reducing greenhouse gases, air and water pollution, and energy consumption. 

[6:0:58,253] Legislation in 2010 (Chapter 15, Statutes of 2010), 2011 (Chapter 9, Statutes of 2011, First Extraordinary Session), and 

[6:1:58,262] 2013 (Chapter 356, Statutes of 2013), authorized financial assistance to encourage energy efficiency retrofits. The Authority 

[6:2:58,271] developed a loan loss reserve program to assist financial institutions in making loans to homeowners in the state for 

[6:3:58,280] residential whole house energy efficiency and renewable energy projects, and developed a risk mitigation program for 

[6:4:58,289] residential Property Assessed Clean Energy programs in California. 

[7:0:58,307] Most recently, the Budget Act of 2014 authorized administration of the California Hub for Energy Efficiency Financing on 

[7:1:58,316] behalf of, and in collaboration with, the California Public Utilities Commission. These energy efficiency financing pilot 

[7:2:58,325] programs will employ various types of credit enhancements to encourage and leverage private capital lending (in both the 

[7:3:58,334] residential and commercial sectors) for energy efficiency improvements needed to help achieve California's energy efficiency 

[7:4:58,343] goals.

[4:0:149,164] 0974 California Pollution Control Financing Authority 

[5:0:58,185] California Pollution Control Financing Authority is committed to stimulating local economies in California by making capital 

[5:1:58,194] more accessible to small businesses, and delivering innovative financing for projects that protect and restore the 

[5:2:58,203] environment. The Authority was created to assist the solid waste, recycling, water, and wastewater industries through its 

[5:3:58,212] Pollution Control Tax-Exempt Bond Program. Over the last twenty years, the Authority has evolved to provide financing 

[5:4:58,221] assistance to California's small business sector through its California Capital Access Program (CalCAP), and to promote the 

[5:5:58,230] reuse and redevelopment of brownfields through the California Recycle Underutilized Sites Program (CALReUSE). 

[5:6:58,248] The Authority consists of the State Treasurer (Chairperson), the State Controller, and the Director of the Department of 

[5:7:58,257] Finance. 

[6:0:58,283] 3-YR EXPENDITURES AND POSITIONS

[16:0:58,281] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[17:0:58,309] 0860 - POLLUTION CONTROL TAX-EXEMPT BOND PROGRAM 

[18:0:58,327] The objective of this program is to provide bond financing to California businesses, irrespective of company size, for the 

[18:1:58,336] acquisition, construction, or installation of qualified pollution control, waste disposal, water furnishing, wastewater treatment, 

[18:2:58,345] waste recovery facilities, and the acquisition and installation of new equipment. Tax-exempt financing issued by the Authority 

[18:3:58,354] assists municipalities in complying with waste diversion mandates of the California Integrated Waste Management Act of 

[18:4:58,363] 1989. As of June 30, 2016, bonds totaling approximately $14.8 billion have been issued by the Authority. 

[19:0:58,381] 0865 - CALIFORNIA CAPITAL ACCESS PROGRAM FOR SMALL BUSINESSES 

[20:0:58,399] The objective of this program is to encourage banks and other financial institutions to make loans to small businesses. 

[20:1:58,408] CalCAP for Small Businesses is a form of loan portfolio insurance that may provide up to 100 percent coverage on certain 

[20:2:58,417] loan defaults. By participating in CalCAP, lenders have available to them a proven financing mechanism to meet the 

[20:3:58,426] financing needs of California's small businesses. The strength of CalCAP rests in its simplicity and its leverage of federal 

[20:4:58,435] and state funds. The program works through the creation of a loan loss-reserve fund for each participating financial 

[20:5:58,444] institution. The Authority funds this reserve together with the financial institution and the borrower. Additional incentives are 

[20:6:58,453] provided to lend to businesses located in specified communities. The reserve serves to reduce loan-loss risk, allowing banks 

[20:7:58,462] to lend to targeted California small businesses. Chapter 731, Statutes of 2010, appropriated $6 million General Fund to 

[20:8:58,471] CalCAP to increase lending efforts. As of June 30, 2016, approximately $3.5 million of the $6 million has been used to assist 

[20:9:58,480] small businesses. 

[21:0:58,498] In addition, California was awarded an allocation of federal funds in the amount of $168.6 million from the federal State 

[21:1:58,507] Small Business Credit Initiative (SSBCI). The Authority and the Governor's Office of Business and Economic Development 

[21:2:58,516] (Go-BIZ) equally share this allocation of $84.3 million each. These funds have enabled the Authority to significantly expand 

[21:3:58,525] the availability of its CalCAP program statewide. The Authority also launched the Collateral Support Program to assist more 

[21:4:58,534] small businesses and utilize the SSBCI Federal funds. Funds were allocated to California in three installments based on 

[21:5:58,543] program progress. The Authority received $27 million in March 2011, $27 million in December 2013, and $29 million in 

[21:6:58,552] August 2015. 

[22:0:58,570] Utilizing the CalCAP model, the Authority has partnered with the Air Resources Board (ARB) to assist diesel truck and 

[22:1:58,579] equipment owners in meeting new clean air requirements by directing a total of $95 million in Air Quality Improvement 

[22:2:58,588] Program funds towards the purchase or retrofit of diesel trucks to comply with ARB's Statewide Truck and Bus Rule. The 

[22:3:58,597] Authority has also partnered with the California Energy Commission to implement a $2 million pilot program to provide credit 

[22:4:58,606] enhancements and rebates to small business borrowers who install electric vehicle charging stations. Similarly, the Authority 

[22:5:58,615] is partnering with the Department of Resources, Recycling, and Recovery to assist with the financing of important state 

[22:6:58,624] recycling objectives. 

[23:0:58,642] 0870 - CALIFORNIA RECYCLE UNDERUTILIZED SITES PROGRAM 

[24:0:58,660] The CALReUSE program assists with the reuse and redevelopment of underutilized properties with real or perceived 

[24:1:58,669] contamination issues (brownfields). CALReUSE addresses a funding and information gap in the development of brownfields 

[24:2:58,678] to help bring these properties into productive reuse. Beginning in 2000, the CALReUSE Assessment Program provided 

[24:3:58,687] forgivable loans of up to $300,000 per brownfield site. The funds assisted with brownfield site assessment and 

[24:4:58,696] characterization, technical assistance, remedial action plans and site access. Eligible projects included sites with potential 

[24:5:58,705] beneficial reuse not currently redeveloped due to lack of information about real or perceived contamination, uncertainty 

[24:6:58,714] about clean-up costs, or concerns regarding time frames and the regulatory process. 

[25:0:58,745] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details. 


# === PAGE 243 === [size: 612x792]
[0:0:58,15] LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE   2017-18 STATE BUDGET — LJE 241 

[1:0:114,44] 0974 California Pollution Control Financing Authority - Continued 

[2:0:58,73] Additionally, Proposition 1C, the Housing and Emergency Shelter Trust Fund Act of 2006, included provisions to fund 

[2:1:58,82] brownfield cleanup that resulted in the expansion of CALReUSE. The CALReUSE Remediation Program received $60 

[2:2:58,91] million in Proposition 1C funds and is providing up to $5 million per project in loans and grants for the purpose of brownfield 

[2:3:58,100] cleanup that promotes infill residential and mixed-used development, including affordable housing, consistent with regional 

[2:4:58,109] and local land use plans. 

[3:0:58,127] 0875 - ALTERNATIVE FINANCING PROGRAMS 

[4:0:58,145] Under its authority to provide alternative methods of financing facilities for pollution control, clean water supply and 

[4:1:58,154] alternative energy production, the Authority is developing alternative financing models to assist sister agencies with 

[4:2:58,163] achieving the state's environmental goals. The Authority is authorized to receive and accept contributions from other sources 

[4:3:58,172] including federal and state agencies to carry out the purposes of its statutory authority. 

[5:0:58,190] 0876 - CALIFORNIA CAPITAL ACCESS PROGRAM FOR COMPLIANCE WITH THE AMERICANS WITH DISABLITIES 

[5:1:58,199] ACT 

[6:0:58,217] The objective of this program, created by Chapter 787, Statutes of 2015, is to help small businesses comply with the federal 

[6:1:58,226] Americans with Disabilities Act and increase access for their employees and customers by encouraging lenders and other 

[6:2:58,235] financial institutions to make loans to very small businesses to finance tenant improvements. The Legislature provided the 

[6:3:58,244] Authority an appropriation of $10 million effective January 1, 2016, to administer a credit enhancement program following the 

[6:4:58,253] CalCAP model and create loan loss reserve accounts for lenders that enroll qualifying loans into the program. 

[6:5:58,271] 0877 - CALIFORNIA SEISMIC SAFETY CAPITAL ACCESS LOAN PROGRAM 

[7:0:58,289] The California Seismic Safety Capital Access Loan Program authorized by Chapter 32, Statutes of 2016, provided a 

[7:1:58,298] one-time allocation of $10 million to provide an accessible loan program to qualified small businesses and residential 

[7:2:58,307] property owners (including multiunit dwellings and mobile homes registered by the California Department of Housing and 

[7:3:58,316] Community Development) for costs related to seismic retrofitting. The Program encourages banks and other financial 

[7:4:58,325] institutions to participate by creating loan loss reserve accounts for lenders that enroll qualifying loans into the program. The 

[7:5:58,334] loans to small businesses and residential property owners are for financing seismic retrofits of real property to reduce losses 

[7:6:58,343] and mitigate seismic damage.

[5:0:152,192] 0977 California Health Facilities Financing Authority 

[5:1:58,212] The mission of the California Health Facilities Financing Authority is to help eligible and credit worthy nonprofit and public 

[5:2:58,221] health facilities reduce their cost of capital, and promote health care improvement and cost containment objectives by 

[5:3:58,230] providing cost-effective tax-exempt bond, low-cost loan, and direct grant programs. 

[6:0:58,248] The Authority was established by Chapter 1033, Statutes of 1979, and consists of nine members: the State Treasurer, the 

[6:1:58,257] Director of the Department of Finance, the State Controller, two public members appointed by the Senate, two public 

[6:2:58,266] members appointed by the Assembly, and two public members appointed by the Governor.

[18:0:58,624] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[19:0:58,651] 0880 - CHILDREN'S HOSPITAL PROGRAM 

[20:0:58,669] In 2004, California voters approved Proposition 61, which established the Children's Hospital Program. In 2008, Proposition 

[20:1:58,678] 3 established the second Children's Hospital Program. The purpose of both programs is to improve the health and welfare 

[20:2:58,687] of California's critically ill children by providing a stable and ready source of funds for capital improvement projects for 

[20:3:58,696] children's hospitals. Children's Hospital Program grant funding is derived from the issuance of general obligation bonds, up 

[20:4:58,705] to $750 million under Proposition 61 and $980 million under Proposition 3. 

[20:5:58,723] 0885 - HEALTH FACILITIES GRANTS AND LOANS

[0:0:58,15] 2017-18 STATE BUDGET — LJE 246   LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE 

[1:0:117,44] 0977 California Health Facilities Financing Authority - Continued 

[2:0:58,82] The Authority serves as a conduit provider of tax-exempt bonds and a direct provider of financial assistance to health 

[2:1:58,91] institutions. 

[2:2:58,109] Tax-Exempt Bond Program 

[3:0:58,127] Bonds issued under this conduit program are not a debt or liability or a pledge of the full faith and credit of the taxing power 

[3:1:58,136] of the state or any of its political subdivisions. The full faith and credit of the participating institutions are pledged for 

[3:2:58,145] repayment of the bonds. To qualify for funding, the proposed project must be a health facility, operated by a private nonprofit 

[3:3:58,154] corporation or association, city, city and county, county, or hospital district. 

[3:4:58,172] Clinic Grant Programs 

[4:0:58,190] Chapter 99, Statutes of 2000 (AB 2875), established the Cedillo-Alarcon Community Clinic Investment Act of 2000 and 

[4:1:58,199] allocated $50 million dollars to the Authority for the purpose of awarding grants to eligible primary care clinics for capital 

[4:2:58,208] outlay projects. In 2004, as part of the Anthem-Well Point merger, $35 million dollars was allocated to the Authority for the 

[4:3:58,217] purpose of awarding grants to eligible health care facilities providing service to underserved communities throughout 

[4:4:58,226] California. To qualify for funding, the proposed project must be a health facility, operated by a private nonprofit corporation 

[4:5:58,235] or association, city, city and county, county, or hospital district. 

[4:6:58,253] HELP II Loan Program 

[5:0:58,271] The Authority administers the Healthcare Expansion Loan Program II (HELP II) to assist small and rural health facilities in 

[5:1:58,280] obtaining financing for their capital needs. The HELP II Program provides two percent and three percent fixed interest rate 

[5:2:58,289] loans of up to $1,500,000 to California's nonprofit small and rural health facilities in an efficient, timely, and cost effective 

[5:3:58,298] manner. The two percent interest rate applies to loans approved from April 30, 2015 - April 30, 2017, and is effective for the 

[5:4:58,307] life of the loan. Refinancing loans are not eligible for the two percent interest rate. Refinancing loans are eligible up to 

[5:5:58,316] $1,000,000. HELP II loans may be used to purchase or construct new facilities, remodel or renovate existing facilities, 

[5:6:58,325] purchase equipment and/or furnishings, and refinance existing debt. 

[5:7:58,343] California Health Access Model Program 

[6:0:58,361] Chapter 23, Statutes of 2012 (AB 1467) authorized the California Health Access Model Program (CHAMP), a grant program 

[6:1:58,370] intended to support innovative methods of delivering health care services and improve health outcomes for vulnerable 

[6:2:58,379] populations and communities by bringing services to individuals where they live or congregate. 

[6:3:58,397] 0890 - MENTAL HEALTH WELLNESS GRANTS 

[7:0:58,415] Chapter 34, Statutes of 2013 (SB 82), the Investment in Mental Health Wellness Act of 2013 and related legislation provided 

[7:1:58,424] $142.5 million in one-time General Fund, and $4 million in ongoing Mental Health Services Act funding to provide grants for 

[7:2:58,433] community based mental health crisis support, which may also be eligible for matching federal funding. 

[7:3:58,451] The Act established a grant program to disburse funds to California counties or to their nonprofit or public agency designates 

[7:4:58,460] for the purpose of developing mental health crisis support programs. Specifically, funds will increase capacity for client 

[7:5:58,469] assistance and services in crisis intervention, crisis stabilization, crisis residential treatment, rehabilitative mental health 

[7:6:58,478] services, and mobile crisis support teams. The grants will support capital improvement, expansion and limited start-up costs.

[4:0:58,139] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[5:0:58,167] 0895 - CALIFORNIA ABLE ACT BOARD 

[6:0:58,185] On December 19, 2014, President Obama signed the Stephen Beck Jr., Achieving a Better Life Experience Act of 2014 (the 

[6:1:58,194] ABLE Act), which allows individuals who became blind or disabled before reaching age 26, to create tax-free savings 

[6:2:58,203] accounts. Individuals can make nondeductible cash contributions to an ABLE account in the name of a specified beneficiary 

[6:3:58,212] with tax-free earnings. ABLE account distributions are also not included in the beneficiary's income, as long as they are 

[6:4:58,221] used for qualified services. Chapter 774, Statutes of 2015 (AB 449), implements the ABLE Act in California, and directs the 

[6:5:58,230] State Treasurer to administer ABLE accounts on behalf of qualified Californians. 

[6:6:58,248] The California Achieving a Better Life Experience Act Board and the California ABLE Program Trust were established by 

[6:7:58,257] Chapter 796, Statutes of 2015 (SB 324), for the purpose of creating a statewide program known as the Qualified ABLE 

[6:8:58,266] Program (the Program). Under the Program, a person may make contributions of up to $100,000 for a taxable year, for the 

[6:9:58,275] benefit of an individual who is an eligible individual for that taxable year, to an ABLE account that is established for the 

[6:10:58,284] purpose of meeting the qualified expenses of the designated beneficiary of the account.

[7:0:183,264] 0985 California School Finance Authority 

[7:1:58,284] The California School Finance Authority (CSFA), created in 1985, provides facilities and working capital financing to school 

[7:2:58,293] districts, community college districts, county offices of education, and charter schools. The State Treasurer serves as chair 

[7:3:58,302] of CSFA and the Superintendent of Public Instruction and the Director of Finance serve as members. CSFA has offices in 

[7:4:58,311] Los Angeles and Sacramento. 

[8:0:58,329] CSFA serves as the primary state agency for California charter schools seeking facility and working capital assistance by 

[8:1:58,338] providing access to low-cost financing through several State and federally funded programs.

[14:0:58,425] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[15:0:58,453] 0918 - SMART BONDS PROGRAM 

[16:0:58,471] Chapter 1438, Statutes of 1985, as amended by Chapter 598, Statutes of 1987, established CSFA and authorized the 

[16:1:58,480] issuance of revenue bonds or other debt instruments. The proceeds from the sale of the bonds were available for loans to 

[16:2:58,489] school and community college districts to assist with the acquisition of equipment and new school sites, construction of new 

[16:3:58,498] facilities, reconstruction of existing facilities, capital improvements, and to provide working capital. Chapter 325, Statutes of 

[16:4:58,507] 2006 (AB 2717), allows CSFA to issue debt on behalf of California charter schools for capital improvements and working 

[16:5:58,516] capital needs. 

[17:0:58,534] 0920 - CHARTER SCHOOL FACILITIES PROGRAM 

[18:0:58,552] Chapter 935, Statutes of 2002, as amended by Chapter 587, Statutes of 2003, created the Charter School Facilities 

[18:1:58,561] Program (CSFP), which provides funding for the new construction, renovation or rehabilitation of charter school facilities. 

[18:2:58,570] CSFA and the Office of Public School Construction jointly administer the program. CSFP was funded through the 

[18:3:58,579] Kindergarten-University Public Education Facilities Bond Acts of 2002, 2004, and 2006, for a total of $900 million. 

[18:4:58,588] Proposition 51, approved by voters in November 2016, extends the existing CSFP and authorized a total of $500 million in 

[18:5:58,597] State General Obligation Bonds for charter school construction projects. 

[19:0:58,615] The program provides a 50 percent state subsidy for the charter school facilities project costs, with the balance of the project 

[19:1:58,624] costs being repaid (to the state) by the charter school in the form of a long-term lease. Recipient charter schools must 

[19:2:58,633] provide site-based instruction, be deemed financially sound by CSFA, and meet other program eligibility requirements. 

[19:3:58,651] 0925 - STATE CHARTER SCHOOL FACILITIES INCENTIVE GRANTS PROGRAM 

[20:0:58,669] In 2004, 2009, and 2014, CSFA was awarded a grant under the United States Department of Education's State Charter 

[20:1:58,678] School Facilities Incentive Grants Program (CFDA 84.282D) to provide California charter schools with assistance for 

[20:2:58,687] facilities costs. Grant funds are used toward a charter school's cost of rent, lease, mortgage or debt service payments for 

[20:3:58,696] existing or new facilities or toward the costs of acquiring land and constructing or renovating a facility. Grants are awarded to 

[20:4:58,705] charter schools based on preference points allotted by the percentage of low-income students, percentage overcrowded, 

[20:5:58,714] not-for-profit status, and demonstrated student performance. Schools cannot use program funds to supplant state funding. 

[21:0:58,745] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[2:0:58,73] 0930 - CHARTER SCHOOL FACILITY GRANT PROGRAM 

[3:0:58,91] The Charter School Facility Grant Program provides Proposition 98 General Fund grants to assist charter schools with rent 

[3:1:58,100] and lease costs. This program targets schools and communities with significant populations of economically disadvantaged 

[3:2:58,109] students. Eligible charter schools are provided up to $750 per unit of eligible average daily attendance, not to exceed 75 

[3:3:58,118] percent of the total annual facilities rent or lease costs.

[8:0:166,449] 0989 California Educational Facilities Authority 

[8:1:58,469] The California Educational Facilities Authority (CEFA) provides qualified nonprofit higher education institutions with 

[9:0:58,478] assistance through a tax-exempt revenue bond program to reduce the costs of financing academic facilities. CEFA may also

[9:2:58,505] CEFA consists of the following five members: the Director of Finance, the State Controller, the State Treasurer, and two

[12:0:58,404] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[13:0:58,431] 0940 - BOND FINANCING 

[14:0:58,449] CEFA issues revenue bonds to assist private educational institutions of higher learning construct educational facilities. 

[14:1:58,458] Because it is authorized to issue tax-exempt bonds, the Authority may be able to provide more favorable financing terms 

[14:2:58,467] than might otherwise be obtainable. CEFA also may include qualifying nonprofit entities as eligible program participants for 

[14:3:58,476] the construction of student and faculty housing. Bonds issued by CEFA are not a debt, liability, or claim on the faith and 

[14:4:58,485] credit or the taxing power of the State of California or any of its political subdivisions. The full faith and credit of the 

[14:5:58,494] participating institution is normally pledged to the payment of the bonds. Bonds issued for this purpose are not subject to the 

[14:6:58,503] state's "private activity" bond ceiling as specified in federal law. 

[15:0:58,521] For purposes of the California Educational Facilities Act, "private college" or "private participating college" means a private 

[15:1:58,530] college that does not restrict the admission of a student based on his or her race or ethnicity, provided that the financing 

[15:2:58,539] does not violate constitutional provisions. 

[16:0:58,557] "Bond" means bonds, notes, debentures, securities, or other evidences of indebtedness. This broad definition allows CEFA 

[16:1:58,566] to issue tax-exempt direct or private placement loans for colleges and universities, which may provide greater cost savings 

[16:2:58,575] than these colleges and universities might otherwise realize on a traditional bond financing. 

[16:3:58,593] 0955 - COLLEGE ACCESS TAX CREDIT FUND 

[17:0:58,611] Chapter 367, Statutes of 2014, required CEFA to administer the College Access Tax Credit Fund and allocate and certify the 

[17:1:58,620] tax credits for taxable years beginning on or after January 1, 2014, and before January 1, 2017. Chapter 22, Statutes of 

[17:2:58,629] 2015, added a requirement that CEFA continue to allocate and certify the tax credits for taxable years beginning on or after 

[17:3:58,638] January 1, 2017, and before January 1, 2018.
